Dawa'i al-Wat' for a Captive Woman (Musabbaya) in Nawadir
States the ruling on dawa'i for a captive slave-girl with reasoning based on absence of claim risk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dawa'i al-wat' for a captive woman and explain the rationale that distinguishes it from a purchased slave-girl.

Core Idea
Dawa'i for a captive woman are not haram because the former owner's claim is not accepted, removing the risk of property confusion.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Nawadir (rare transmissions) regarding dawa'i (aphrodisiacs) for a captive slave-girl (musabbaya). While the general rule prohibits conjugal relations before istibra', the permissibility of dawa'i depends on the risk of mixing lineages. Here, Imam Muhammad provides the reason why the risk is absent, distinguishing captives from purchased slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general context
The passage addresses dawa'i (medications intended to induce desire) for a musabbaya, a female captive taken in jihad who becomes a slave-girl. Dawa'i are normally allowed, but the question arises due to the prohibition of intercourse before istibra'.
Dawa'i are distinct from actual intercourse; they do not require istibra' but may be restricted if they create lineage confusion.
2
Recognize the authority level of the ruling
This ruling is from the Nawadir, specifically transmitted from Imam Muhammad, not from the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. This means it is a rare transmission and carries less authority than the established sources.
Nawadir are considered supplementary; fatwa typically relies on Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the rationale for permissibility
The key reason given is that there is no possibility (la tahtamil) of the dawa'i occurring in the property of another (ghayr al-milk). If pregnancy results from such dawa'i, the claim of the former harbi (enemy) owner is not accepted in Islamic law.
The harbi's claim is rejected because he is a non-Muslim enemy and the child belongs to the current owner.
4
Contrast with the purchased slave-girl case
Imam Muhammad draws a comparison (qiyas) with a purchased slave-girl (al-mushtara). For a purchased slave-girl, dawa'i are haram because the seller's claim of pregnancy is valid and can create uncertainty about ownership.
The distinction lies in the legal validity of the former owner's claim: accepted for purchased slaves, rejected for captives.
5
Derive the final ruling
Based on the absence of risk, the ruling is that dawa'i are mubah (permissible) for the captive woman. The passage does not mention any conditions or restrictions beyond this general permissibility.
This ruling is specific to captives taken in jihad and does not apply to other categories of slave-girls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسبیہ ( گرفتار ) سے دوائی وطی کا حکم.
ولم يذكر الدواعى فى المسبية وعن محمد انها لا تحرم لانها لا تحتمل وقوعها في غير الملك لانه لو ظهر بها حبل لاتصح دعوة الحربي بخلاف المشتراة على مابينا .
ترجمہ اور دوائی کا مسبیہ کے بارے میں ( ظاہر الروایۃ میں ) ذکر نہیں کیا گیا اور محمد سے منقول ہے کہ دوائی حرام نہیں ہیں اسلئے کہ ان کے غیر ملک میں وقوع کا احتمال نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اگر اس کو عمل ظاہر ہو گیا تو حربی کا دعوی صحیح نہیں ہے بخلاف مشراۃ کے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔
تشریح جس عورت کو گرفتار کیا گیا اور وہ کسی مجاہد کے حصہ میں آگئی تو استبراء سے پہلے اس سے وطی کرنا جائز نہیں لیکن دوائی وطی کا کیا حکم ہے اس سلسلے میں ظاہر الرویۃہ میں کچھ مذکور نہیں ہے لیکن نوادر میں امام محمد سے منقول ہے کہ دوائی حرام نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں دوائی وطی میں یہ احتمال نہیں ہے کہ وہ غیر کی ملک میں واقع ہو جائیں اسلئے کہ اگر یہاں حمل بھی ظاہر ہو جائے تو اس کے حربی شوہر کا دعوی مسموع نہ ہوگا اور مشتراة میں بائع کا دعوی مقبول اور مسموع ہوگا۔ (کما مر )
Ruling on dawa'i for a captive woman (musabbaya). And the dawa'i are not mentioned in (the case of) the captive woman, and it is reported from Muhammad that they are not haram because there is no possibility of their occurrence in the property of another, for if pregnancy becomes apparent in her, the claim of the harbi (enemy) is not accepted, unlike the purchased one according to what we have explained. Translation: And the ruling on dawa'i for the captive woman is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is narrated from Muhammad that they are not haram because there is no possibility of their occurrence in the property of another. Because if pregnancy becomes apparent in her, the claim of the harbi is not valid, unlike the purchased one for the same reason we have explained. Explanation: A woman who is captured and comes into the share of a mujahid: intercourse before istibra' is not permissible, but what is the ruling on dawa'i? In Zahir al-Riwayah, nothing is mentioned on this, but in Nawadir, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that dawa'i are not haram because here there is no possibility that they will occur in the property of another, for even if pregnancy appears, the claim of her harbi husband is not heard, whereas in the purchased slave-girl, the seller's claim is accepted and heard. (As mentioned before.)
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for dawa'i al-wat' in the case of a captive woman (musabbaya) who becomes the property of a mujahid. The ruling is not found in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, but from the Nawadir (rare transmissions), Imam Muhammad reports that dawa'i are not haram. The reason is that even if pregnancy occurs, the claim of the former non-Muslim owner (harbi) is not accepted in Islamic law, unlike the case of a purchased slave-girl where the seller's claim is valid. Thus, the risk of property confusion does not exist here, so dawa'i remain permissible. This shows that the prohibition for the purchased slave-girl was specifically due to the seller's potential claim, which creates uncertainty about ownership. In captives, there is no such risk, so dawa'i are not forbidden.

Key Terms
مسبیہ (musabbaya): A female captive taken in jihad who becomes a slave-girl by virtue of being part of the spoils.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare transmissions from the early Hanafi imams, not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
دوائی وطی (dawa'i al-wat'): Medications or substances used to increase sexual desire.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim enemy combatant; his legal claims are not recognized in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad's narration in Nawadir, why are dawa'i al-wat' not haram for a captive woman (musabbaya) as they are for a purchased slave-girl?
A) Istibra' is not required for captive women.
B) The former owner (harbi) is not alive to make a claim.
C) The harbi husband's claim of pregnancy is not accepted in Islamic law.
D) Captive women are not subject to ownership rules.

Key Takeaway
Dawa'i al-wat' for a captive woman are permissible because the harbi former owner's claim is legally rejected, eliminating the risk of lineage confusion that prohibits dawa'i in purchased slave-girls.

Istibra' for Pregnant and Non-Menstruating Slave Women
Ruling on istibra' for pregnant and non-menstruating slaves with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of istibra' for pregnant and non-menstruating slave women, and explain the proof and analogy to 'iddah.

Core Idea
A pregnant slave's istibra' ends at birth; a non-menstruating slave's istibra' is one month, analogized to 'iddah but shorter.

Istibra' is a wajib waiting period required before a new master can have intercourse with a purchased slave-girl, ensuring she is not pregnant from the previous owner. The method varies: pregnant slaves complete istibra' by giving birth, while non-menstruating slaves (minors or post-menopausal) complete it by waiting one month. This lesson examines the evidence from the hadith and the qiyas (analogy) to the 'iddah of a free woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage divides slave women into two groups: those who are pregnant (al-hubala) and those who do not menstruate (dhawat al-ashhur), such as minors or elderly women. Identify which category each ruling applies to.
The category 'dhawat al-ashhur' literally means 'those with months' — women who count their waiting period by months due to absence of menstruation.
2
State the ruling for each
For a pregnant slave, istibra' is completed by delivery; for a non-menstruating slave, it is completed by the passage of one month.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they give birth, nor with non-pregnant until they have completed one menstruation' is cited. For the pregnant, the hadith directly indicates delivery. For non-menstruating, the absence of menstruation necessitates a substitute — months — by analogy to 'iddah.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but accepted as proof for this ruling.
4
Understand the analogy (qiyas) to 'iddah
The analogy is to the 'iddah of a non-menstruating free woman, who waits three months. However, for istibra', one month suffices because the purpose is simply to confirm absence of pregnancy, not to observe mourning or other obligations.
The shorter duration is based on istihsan (juristic preference), recognizing the lighter purpose of istibra' compared to 'iddah.
5
Note the practical difference
A common misconception is that non-menstruating slaves must wait three months like in 'iddah. But the Hanafi school holds that one month is sufficient, as the underlying rationale (ta'qib al-bara'ah) is achieved sooner.
This ruling is consistent across the school with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاستبراء فى الحامل بوضع الحمل لما روينا وفى ذوات الاشهر بالاشهر لانه اقيم في حقهن مقام الحيض كما في المعتدة
ترجمہ اور حاملہ میں استبراء وضع حمل کے ساتھ ہوگا اس دلیل سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور مہینہ والیوں میں مہینہ کے ساتھ اسلئے کہ مہینہ ان کے حق میں حیض کے قائم مقام ہے جیسے معتدہ کے اندر۔
تشریح جس باندی کو حمل ہے اس کا استبراء وضع حمل سے ہو گا اس کی دلیل ماقبل میں روایت کردہ حدیث ہے یعنی الا لا تـــوطــــا الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الجيالى حتى يستبرئن بحيضة اور جو صغیرہ یا آئہ ہے ان کا استبراء ایک مہینہ سے ہوگا کیونکہ ان کے حق میں مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے جیسے وہ عورت جو عدت طلاق گزارے اور اس کو حیض نہ آتا ہو تو وہ مہینوں سے عدت گزارتی ہے ایسے ہی یہاں ہوگا۔
And istibra' for the pregnant one is by giving birth, according to what we narrated; and for those with months (non-menstruating) it is by months, because months are established in their case as a substitute for menstruation, just as in the case of the woman in 'iddah. Translation: For a pregnant slave-girl, istibra' is by giving birth, based on the hadith we narrated; for those who count months, istibra' is by months because months are the substitute for menstruation, just as in 'iddah. Explanation: A slave-girl who is pregnant – her istibra' is by delivery, and the proof is the hadith narrated previously: 'Indeed, do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they give birth, nor with non-pregnant until they have completed one menstruation.' And for a minor or a post-menopausal woman, their istibra' is by one month because months are the substitute for menstruation, just like a woman undergoing 'iddah after divorce who does not menstruate completes her 'iddah by months. Similarly here.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on how istibra' (the waiting period before a new master can have intercourse with a slave-girl) is performed for different types of slave women. For a pregnant slave-girl, istibra' is completed by giving birth—this is based on the well-known hadith: 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they give birth.' For those who do not menstruate, such as a minor girl (saghira) or a post-menopausal woman (a'isa), istibra' is performed by waiting one month. This is analogous to the 'iddah period for a free woman who does not menstruate; in 'iddah, she waits three months by analogy, but for istibra' one month suffices. The principle is that months substitute for menstrual cycles when menstruation is absent. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school and is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
وضع حمل (wada' haml): Giving birth; the completion of pregnancy by delivery.
ذوات الاشهر (dhawat al-ashhur): Women who do not menstruate (minors, post-menopausal) and thus perform istibra' by months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof cited for the ruling that a pregnant slave's istibra' is completed by delivery?
A) A Quranic verse prohibiting intercourse with pregnant women.
B) A hadith: 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they give birth.'
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Qiyas to the 'iddah of a free woman.

Key Takeaway
A pregnant slave's istibra' is completed by birth, and a non-menstruating slave's istibra' is one month, based on hadith and analogy to 'iddah with adjustment for purpose.

Effect of Menses During Monthly Istibra' and Ruling for Mumtad al-Tuhr
Explains two rulings: monthly istibra' voided by menses, and no fixed period for mumtad al-tuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that when the original method for istibra' becomes available, the substitute method is void, and state the ruling for a slave-girl with prolonged tuhr.

Core Idea
If menses occurs during monthly istibra', the count is void; she must observe one menstrual period. For prolonged tuhr, wait without a fixed period.

This lesson examines two scenarios in Hanafi fiqh regarding istibra' of slave-girls: when monthly istibra' is interrupted by sudden menstruation, and when a slave-girl has prolonged purity (mumtad al-tuhr). The ruling hinges on the principle that original methods take precedence over substitutes. The passage also highlights the Zahir al-Riwayah's refusal to set a fixed duration for mumtad al-tuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two distinct cases: (1) a slave-girl performing istibra' by months who menstruates during that period, and (2) a slave-girl whose menses becomes prolonged (mumtad al-tuhr). Understand what triggers each ruling.
The first scenario is about a slave-girl who is not menstruating initially but then menstruates; the second about one who never menstruates.
2
Understand the qiyas with 'iddah
The passage analogizes to the 'iddah of a free woman: if a woman performing 'iddah by months menstruates, she must switch to menstrual cycles. The same principle applies to istibra'. Recognize the shared illa: availability of the original method before the objective is achieved through the substitute.
The illa is 'ability to use the original'.
3
Apply the principle 'original over substitute'
When the original method (menstruation) becomes available before the waiting period is complete, the substitute (months) is void. Derive the ruling that the monthly istibra' is void and she must complete one full menstrual period.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
4
Recognize the Hanafi flexibility for mumtad al-tuhr
For a slave-girl whose menses stops for a long time, there is no fixed istibra' period in Zahir al-Riwayah. The master must wait until it becomes clear she is not pregnant. Note that later Hanafi scholars may prescribe a maximum (e.g., nine months) based on istihsan.
The text explicitly says 'no estimation in Zahir al-Riwayah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حاضت في اثنائه بطل الاستبراء بالايام للقدرة على الاصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبدل كما في العدة فان ارتفع حيضها تركها حتى اذا تبين انها ليست بحامل وقع عليها وليس فيه تقدير في ظاهر الرواية
ترجمہ اور جبکہ مہینہ کے بیچ میں اس کو حیض آجائے تو ایام سے استبراء باطل ہو گیا اصل کے اوپر قدرت کی وجہ سے بدل کے ذریعہ حصول مقصود سے پہلے جیسے عورت میں۔ پس اگر اس کا حیض مرتفع ہو جائے (ممتد ہو جائے ) تو اس کو چھوڑے رکھے ( وطی نہ کرے ) یہاں تک کہ جب یہ ظاہر ہو جائے کہ وہ حاملہ نہیں ہے تو اس سے وطی کرنے اور اس میں ظاہر الروایۃ میں کوئی تقدیر نہیں ہے۔
تشریح وہ باندی جس کو حیض نہیں مہینہ سے استبراء کر رہی تھی کہ درمیان میں اس کو اتفاق سے حیض آگیا تو اب استبراء حیض سے ہوگا اور ایام سے جو استبراء اس نے کیا وہ باطل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ جب بدل سے حصول مقصد سے پہلے پہلے اصل کے اوپر قدرت ہو جائے تو وہاں یہی حکم ہوا کرتا ہے۔ لہذا عورت میں بھی یہی ہے کہ عورت مہینوں سے عدت گزار رہی تھی کہ درمیان عدت اس کو حیض آگیا تو اب عدت حیض سے گزارنا واجب ہو گیا۔ باندی ممتدة الطبر ہے تو اس میں کیا کیا جائے تو فرمایا کہ اس سے وطی نہ کرے۔ ہاں جب ظاہر ہو جائے کہ اس کو حمل نہیں ہے اب اس سے وطی کر سکتا ہے۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ یہ کتنی مدت میں ظاہر ہوگا تو ظاہر الروایۃ میں اسکی کوئی تعیین نہیں ہے۔
And if she menstruates during it (the monthly period), the istibra' by days becomes void because of the ability to use the original (menstruation) before achieving the purpose through the substitute, just as in 'iddah. Then if her menses ceases (prolonged), he leaves her (does not have intercourse) until it becomes clear that she is not pregnant, then he may have intercourse with her, and there is no fixed period in Zahir al-Riwayah. Translation: And when during the monthly period she menstruates, then the istibra' by days becomes void because of the ability to use the original before achieving the purpose through the substitute, as in the case of a woman in 'iddah. So if her menses becomes prolonged (i.e., she becomes mumtad al-tuhr), he leaves her (refrains from intercourse) until it becomes apparent that she is not pregnant, then he may have intercourse, and there is no fixed period in Zahir al-Riwayah. Explanation: A slave-girl who was doing istibra' by months because she did not menstruate – if she happens to menstruate during that period, then now istibra' will be by menstruation, and the istibra' by days that she did is void. Because when one is able to use the original (menstruation) before achieving the objective through the substitute, this is the ruling. Similarly in 'iddah: a woman performing 'iddah by months, if she menstruates during that period, she must complete 'iddah by menstruation. For a slave-girl with prolonged tuhr (mumtad al-tuhr), what should be done? He said: do not have intercourse with her. Yes, when it becomes clear that she is not pregnant, then he may have intercourse. Now, as for how long it will take to become clear, there is no fixed period in Zahir al-Riwayah.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios within the topic of istibra' by months for non-menstruating slaves. First, if during the monthly waiting period the slave-girl suddenly menstruates, the monthly istibra' becomes void. She must then complete istibra' by observing one menstrual period, because the original means (menstruation) has become available. This is analogous to 'iddah: if a woman performing 'iddah by months menstruates, she must switch to 'iddah by menstrual cycles. The principle is that when the original becomes available, the substitute is abandoned. Second, for a slave-girl whose menses stops for a long time (mumtad al-tuhr), meaning she does not menstruate for an extended period but is not post-menopausal, there is no fixed duration for istibra' in the Zahir al-Riwayah. The master must wait until it is reasonably clear that she is not pregnant. This could be determined by physical signs or, according to some later Hanafi scholars, a period of nine months (the maximum pregnancy duration) or a similar approximation. However, the text explicitly states that no specific time is prescribed in the core texts, leaving room for ijtihad.

Key Terms
ممتدة الطهر (mumtad al-tuhr): A woman whose interval between menstrual periods becomes very long or indefinite, such that she does not menstruate for many months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a slave-girl who is performing istibra' by one month suddenly menstruates during that month?
A) She continues the monthly count and ignores the menses.
B) The monthly istibra' is void, and she must now observe one menstrual period.
C) She must restart the entire month from the beginning.
D) Istibra' is complete immediately because she menstruated.

Key Takeaway
Menstruation during monthly istibra' voids the substitute; for prolonged tuhr, wait without a fixed period in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Prohibition of Intimacy for Muṭahar Until Expiation
Explains prohibition of wathi and its means for muṭahar with exception for haid and sawm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muṭahar regarding intercourse and its means, explain the general principle that the cause of the haram is haram, and identify the exception for menstruation and fasting with its proof from istihsan and prophetic practice.

Core Idea
For a muṭahar, intercourse and its means are haram until expiation, but allowed during menstruation and fasting due to istihsan.

Zihar is an early form of divorce where a husband declares his wife like his mother, making intercourse forbidden until he expiates. This lesson examines the ruling on physical intimacy for a muṭahar (the one who declared zihar) and explores a key legal principle: the means to a forbidden act are also forbidden. But is this principle absolute? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer, showing how necessity and hardship can override the general rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Read the first part of the passage: it states that for the muṭahar, intercourse and all means leading to it (touching, kissing, looking with desire) are forbidden until expiation. Identify the act and the timeframe.
The ruling applies only before expiation; after expiation, normal marital relations resume.
2
Extract the general principle
The passage gives the principle: 'the cause of the haram is haram' (al-asl anna sabab al-haram haram). This means anything that necessarily leads to a forbidden act is itself forbidden, analogous to i'tikaf and ihram.
This principle is a form of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking the means to evil).
3
Analyze the exception
The passage asks: why is this principle not applied to menstruation and fasting? The answer: because these conditions last long (half a woman's life for menses, a month or more for fasting), and forbidding means would cause undue hardship (haraj).
The exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship.
4
Examine the proof
The passage cites a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss while fasting and lie down with his wives during menstruation. This shows that the means are permitted despite the main act being forbidden.
The hadith provides a direct precedent, overriding the general principle.

Source Text

كفارہ ظہار ادا کرنے والے کیلئے اپنی بیوی سے وطی اور دوائی وطی حرام ہے

قال ولا يقرب المظاهر ولا يلمس ولا يقبل ولا ينظر الى فرجها بشهوة حتى يكفر لانه لما حرم الوطى الى ان يكفر حرم الدواعى للافضاء اليه لان الاصل ان سبب الحرام حرام كما في الاعتكاف والاحرام وفى المنكوحة اذا وطئت بشبهة

ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ اور مظاہر جماع نہیں کرے گا اور نہ چھوئے گا اور نہ بوسہ لے گا اور نہ شہوت کے ساتھ اس کی شرمگاہ کی جانب دیکھے گا یہاں تک کہ کفارہ ادا کر دے اسلئے کہ کفارہ دینے تک جب وطی حرام ہے تو دواعی حرام ہیں (ان کے) وطی تک مفضی ہونے کی وجہ سے اسلئے کہ قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ حرام کا سبب حرام ہے جیسے اعتکاف میں اور احرام میں اور منکوحہ میں جبکہ وہ شبہہ کے ساتھ وطی کر لی گئی ہو۔

تشریح جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے ظہار کیا ہے تو کفارہ دینے سے پہلے مظاہر کو جائز نہیں کہ وہ اس عورت سے وطی کرے اسی طرح دوائی ولی بھی سب کے سب حرام ہوں گے تاکہ دوائی مفضی الی الوطی نہ بن جائیں اور قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ حرام کا سبب بھی حرام ہوتا ہے تو جب وطی حرام تو اس کے دوائی بھی حرام ہوں گے جیسے اعتکاف میں وطی حرام ہے تو دوائی وطی بھی حرام ہوں گے اور حالت احرام میں مجرم کیلئے وطی حلال نہیں تو دوائی وطی بھی حلال نہیں ہوں گے اور اگر کسی کی بیوی سے کسی شہر میں وطی کر لی یعنی اپنی بیوی یا اپنی باندی سمجھ کر تو وہ عدت گزارے گی اور عدت گزرنے سے پہلے اس کا شوہر اس سے وہلی نہیں کرے گا اور نہ دوائی وطی حلال ہیں ۔

سوال کا جواب

بخلاف حالة الحيض والصوم لان الحيض يمتد شطر عمرها والصوم يمتد شهراً فرضاً واكثر العمر نفلا ففى المنع عنها بعض الحرج ولا كذالك ما عددناها لقصور مددها وقد صح ان النبي عليه السلام كان يقبل وهو صائم ويضاجع نساءه وهن حيض.

ترجمہ بخلاف حالت حیض کے اور روزہ کے اسلئے کہ حیض ممتد ہوتا ہے اس کی عمر کے نصف میں اور روزہ ممتد ہوتا ہے ایک مہینہ تک فرض کے طور پر اور عمر کے اکثر حصہ میں نفلی طور پر تو دوائی سے منع کرنے میں کچھ حرج ہے اور جن کو ہم نے شمار کرایا ہے وہ ایسے نہیں ہیں ان کی مدتوں کے کم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ بات درجۂ صحت کو پہنچی ہوئی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام روزہ کی حالت میں بوسہ لیا کرتے اور اپنی بیویوں کے پاس لیٹتے تھے حالانکہ وہ حائضہ ہوتی تھیں۔

تشریح یہاں یہ سوال ہو رہا تھا کہ جب قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ حرام کا سبب بھی حرام ہوتا ہے تو پھر حالت حیض میں اور روزہ میں وطی حرام ہے لیکن دوائی وطی حرام نہیں ہیں؟ تو فرمایا کہ چونکہ حیض تو کم و بیش عورت کو عمر کے نصف حصہ میں آتا رہتا ہے اور اسی طرح روزہ کی مدت اگر وہ فرض ہو تو ایک ماہ ہے اور نفلی ہو تو عمر کا اکثر حصہ ہے تو اگر یہاں دوائی سے منع کر دیا جاتا تو حرج کثیر لازم آتا اور پہلی صورت میں یہ بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کی مدتیں کم ہیں اور حدیث میں بھی آیا ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم روزہ کی حالت میں بوسہ لیا کرتے تھے اور حالت حیض میں ازواج مطہرات کے پاس لیٹ جاتے تھے۔
For the one who performs zihar, intercourse and the means to intercourse with his wife are forbidden. He said: The muṭahar should not have intercourse, nor touch, nor kiss, nor look at her private parts with desire until he makes expiation, because when intercourse is forbidden until expiation, the means leading to it are also forbidden, since the principle is that the cause of the forbidden is forbidden, as in i'tikaf and ihram, and in the case of a married woman who has intercourse under a misapprehension. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The muṭahar will not have intercourse, nor touch, nor kiss, nor look at her private parts with desire until he performs expiation, because when intercourse is forbidden until expiation, the means are forbidden due to leading to it, because the general rule is that the cause of the forbidden is forbidden, as in i'tikaf and ihram, and in the married woman when she has intercourse under a misapprehension. Commentary: The person who has declared zihar against his wife is not permitted to have intercourse with her before expiation; similarly, all means to intercourse are forbidden so that they do not lead to intercourse. The general rule is that the cause of prohibition is also prohibited. So when intercourse is forbidden, its means are also forbidden, as in i'tikaf where intercourse is forbidden, so its means are also forbidden; and in ihram, intercourse is not permissible for a pilgrim, so its means are also not permissible. And if someone's wife has intercourse in a state of misapprehension (thinking she was his wife or slave), she completes her 'iddah, and before that, her husband cannot have intercourse with her, nor are the means to intercourse permissible. Answer to a question: It is different in the case of menstruation and fasting, because menstruation extends over half her life, and fasting extends over a month as an obligation and most of life as supererogatory; thus prohibiting the means would involve some hardship, not like what we counted because their durations are short. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss while fasting and lie down with his wives while they were menstruating. Translation: It is different in the case of menstruation and fasting because menstruation extends over half her life, and fasting extends over a month as an obligation and most of life as supererogatory, so prohibiting the means would involve hardship, and those we enumerated are not like that because their durations are short. And it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss while fasting and lie down with his wives while they were menstruating. Commentary: Here a question arises: when the general rule is that the cause of the forbidden is also forbidden, then why in menstruation and fasting are intercourse forbidden but means to intercourse not forbidden? He answers: Since menstruation comes upon a woman for about half her life, and fasting, if obligatory, is for a month, and if supererogatory, for most of life, so if means were prohibited here, great hardship would result, whereas in the first case, it is not so because their durations are short. And it is narrated in hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss while fasting and lie down with his pure wives during menstruation.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the prohibitions on a man who has declared zihar against his wife. It is a ruling with proof. The author first states the ruling: the man cannot have intercourse, nor touch, kiss, or look at her private parts with desire until he performs expiation. The proof is the principle that the cause of the haram is also haram, analogous to the rules in i'tikaf and ihram. The commentary then addresses a potential objection: if this principle is universal, why is it not applied to menstruation and fasting? The answer is that applying it there would cause undue hardship because those conditions last long, so the Prophet's practice allows kissing and lying together, showing istihsan overrides the general principle. The passage ends with the hadith proof.

Key Terms
مظاهر (muṭahar): The husband who has declared zihar (an early form of divorce) against his wife.
دوائی وطی (dawā'ī al-wathi): The means or acts leading to intercourse, such as touching, kissing, and looking with desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because menstruation and fasting are not true prohibitions.
B) Because the durations are long, and prohibiting the means would cause undue hardship.
C) Because the Prophet disliked those acts.
D) Because the wife's consent overrides the rule.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the means to intercourse during long-duration prohibitions like menstruation and fasting to avoid hardship, based on istihsan and prophetic practice.

Prohibition of Intimacy with Two Slave Sisters
Ruling with Quranic proof on collecting between two slave sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master who kisses both his slave sisters with desire, and explain the Quranic proof and the condition that allows subsequent intimacy.

Core Idea
Kissing both slave sisters with desire triggers the same prohibition as intercourse—removal of one is required.

This lesson presents a detailed ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir on a man who owns two slave sisters and kisses both with desire. The ruling clarifies that such an act constitutes 'collecting' between the sisters in the sense of intimacy, which is explicitly prohibited by the Quran. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the conditions under which the prohibition can be lifted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a master kissing both his slave sisters with desire. Determine the legal classification (hukm) of this act and its consequence for the master's subsequent intimate acts.
The ruling is that the master becomes prohibited from any intercourse, kissing with desire, touching with desire, or looking at private parts with desire of either slave sister.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary source of proof cited by the author. The passage explicitly references the Quranic verse 4:23: 'And do not collect between two sisters.'
The dalil is a direct Quranic prohibition (nahy), which in Hanafi usul indicates haram.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse proves the ruling. The general prohibition of 'collecting' (jam') between sisters covers both marriage and intercourse, and by extension, any act that leads to or implies intimacy, such as kissing with desire.
The imperative prohibition is qat'i in thubut and dalala, so it overrides any permissive interpretation of the verse 'or what your right hands possess' (4:24).
4
Note the condition for lifting the prohibition
Identify what must be done for the master to regain permissibility with one of the sisters. The passage states that he must remove ownership of one sister through sale, marriage, or freeing.
Once one sister's 'private part' (i.e., her sexual availability) is transferred to another, the remaining sister becomes permissible for him.
5
Recognize exceptions and nuances
Consider cases where only one sister is kissed, or where the kiss is without desire. The commentary clarifies that kissing without desire is treated as non-existent, and kissing only one sister only prohibits that one.
This step ensures precise application of the ruling.

Source Text

قال ومن له امتان اختان فقبلهما بشهوة فانه لا يجامع واحدة منهما ولا يقبلها ولا يمسها بشهوة ولا ينظر ا بشهوة حتى يملك فرج الاخرى غيره بملک او نکاح او یعتقها

ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ جس کی دوباندی بہنیں ہوں پس اس نے ان دونوں کا شہوت سے بوسہ لیا تو وہ ان دونوں میں سے کسی سے جماع نہیں کرے گا اور نہ کسی ایک کا بوسہ لیگا اور نہ اس کو چھوئے گا اور نہ اس کی شرمگاہ کی جانب دیکھے، یہاں تک کہ مالک بنا دے دوسری کی فرج کا اپنے غیر کو ملک کے ساتھ یا نکاح کے ساتھ یا اس کو آزاد کر دے۔

تنبیہ اگر اس نے صرف ایک کا بوسہ لیا تو اس سے وہی جائز ہے نہ کہ دوسری سے نیز اگر بوسہ شہوت کے ساتھ نہ ہوتو وہ عدم کے درجہ میں ہے۔

دو مملوکہ بہنوں کو باعتبار وطی جمع کرنا جائز نہیں

واصل هذان الجمع بين الاختين المملوكتين لا يجوز وطيا لاطلاق قوله تعالى وان تجمعوابين الاختين ولا يعارض بقوله تعالى او ما ملكت ايمانكم لان الترجيح للمحرم

The one who has two slave sisters, and kissed both with desire, he should not have intercourse with either, nor kiss her, nor touch her with desire, nor look at her private parts with desire, until he makes the private part of the other owned by someone else through ownership, marriage, or freeing her. He said: Whoever has two slave sisters, and kissed both with desire, then he should not have intercourse with either of them, nor kiss her, nor touch her with desire, nor look at her private parts with desire, until he makes the private part of the other owned by someone else through ownership, marriage, or freeing her. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever has two slave sisters, and he kissed both with desire, then he will not have intercourse with either, nor kiss either, nor touch her, nor look at her private parts with desire, until he makes the private part of the other owned by someone else through ownership, marriage, or freeing her. Commentary: The Quranic text prohibits collecting between two sisters, both in marriage and in intercourse, and kissing with desire etc. is in the ruling of intercourse. So when a master has two slave sisters in his ownership and he kisses both with desire, he has now collected between them in intimacy. Therefore, he cannot have intercourse with either, nor kiss with desire, nor touch, nor look at the private parts with desire. However, if he transfers ownership of one of them, or marries her off, or frees her, then intercourse with the other becomes permissible. Note: If he only kissed one, then that one is permissible, not the other. Also, if kissing is not with desire, it is treated as nonexistent. It is not permissible to collect between two owned sisters in terms of intercourse. The basis of this is that collecting between two sisters who are both owned is not permissible for intercourse due to the generality of Allah's statement, "And do not collect between two sisters," and it is not opposed by His statement, "Or what your right hands possess," because preference is given to the prohibition. Translation: The basis of this is that collecting between two sisters who are both owned is not permissible for intercourse due to the generality of Allah's statement, "And do not collect between two sisters," and it will not be opposed by the command "Or what your right hands possess" because preference is given to the prohibited. Commentary: Now he states the proof for the mentioned ruling: that Allah's statement "And do not collect between two sisters" is general, and in it...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the ruling on a man who owns two slave sisters. It is a ruling with proof. The author first presents the ruling: if the master kisses both slave sisters with desire, he becomes prohibited from any intercourse, kissing, touching, or looking at the private parts of either, until he removes ownership of one of them (by sale, marriage, or freeing). The reason is that the act of kissing both with desire constitutes 'collecting' between them in the sense of intimacy, which is prohibited by the Quranic verse "Do not collect between two sisters" (4:23). The commentary adds a note: if only one is kissed, the prohibition does not apply to her; and if the kiss is without desire, it is as if nothing happened. The proof is that the Quranic prohibition is general over all forms of 'collecting,' including intercourse and its means, and the verse "Or what your right hands possess" (4:24) does not override it because the prohibition takes precedence.

Key Terms
امتان اختان (amtan ukhtan): Two slave women who are biological sisters.
وطی (wathi): Sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must marry both.
D) He must simply wait for a month.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic prohibition of collecting between sisters covers both marriage and ownership, and even kissing with desire triggers the ban until one sister is removed from the owner's reach.

The Hanafi Ruling on Men Kissing and Embracing
States the Hanafi ruling and an intra-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man kissing another man, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Kissing and embracing between men is makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school, though Abu Yusuf permitted it based on the Prophet's example.

This passage from Kitab al-Karahiyya addresses physical affection between men—specifically kissing and embracing. The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) considers these actions makruh, but Abu Yusuf disagrees, citing a prophetic precedent. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between different levels of evidence within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Locate the specific act being ruled upon: a man kissing another man's mouth, hand, or any part, and embracing. Note that the ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text explicitly says 'yukrahu' (it is disliked).
2
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The passage states that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the makruh view, while Abu Yusuf considers it permissible (la ba'sa). Recognize that this is a disagreement within the Hanafi school.
Abu Yusuf is one of the Sahibayn, so this is a significant difference.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf cites a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) embraced Ja'far ibn Abi Talib. Understand that he uses this as evidence that embracing is permissible.
The hadith is ahad (solitary) and zanni al-thubut, but Abu Yusuf treats it as probative.
4
Recognize the relied-upon position
Al-Tahawi reports that the makruh view is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. In later Hanafi fatwa, this is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
The passage cuts off before the full response, but the tarjih is implied by reporting the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرد کیلئے مرد کے منہ ، ہاتھ اور کسی چیز کا بوسہ لینا اور معانقہ کرنے کا حکم وبكره ان يقبل الرجل فم الرجل اويده او شيأ منه او يعانقه وذكر الطحاوى ان هذا قول ابي حنيفه و محمد وقال ابو يوسف رحمهم الله لا بأس بالتقبيل والمعانقة لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام عائق جعفرا رضى الله
The ruling on a man kissing the mouth of a man, or his hand, or any part of him, and embracing him. And it is makruh for a man to kiss the mouth of a man, or his hand, or any part of him, or to embrace him. And al-Tahawi mentioned that this is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said: There is no harm in kissing and embracing, because of the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) embraced Ja'far (may Allah be pleased with him)...
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Karahiyya addresses the legal ruling on physical affection between men. The relied-upon position according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that it is makruh (disliked) for a man to kiss another man's mouth, hand, or any other part, and also to embrace him. This is considered a form of unnecessary intimacy. However, Abu Yusuf disagrees and considers it permissible, citing the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) embraced Ja'far ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) upon his return from Abyssinia. The text cuts off, but likely continues with a response. The ruling is based on the principle of avoiding excessive physical contact that may resemble immoral acts.

Key Terms
تقبيل (taqbil): Kissing, specifically between men, which is the subject of the disliked ruling.
معانقة (mu'anaqah): Embracing, physical hugging between men.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but is better to avoid. In Hanafi fiqh, it can be tanzihi (close to permissible) or tahrimi (close to haram), but here it is likely tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which Hanafi imam considered it permissible (la ba'sa) for a man to kiss and embrace another man?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Abu Yusuf
D) Al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally rules that a man kissing or embracing another man is makruh (disliked), though Abu Yusuf permitted it based on the Prophet's action; the mufta bihi is the majority view.

Buying from a Seller Claiming Agency: Reliance on Statement
Ruling on buying a known slave-girl from a seller claiming agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a buyer may rely on a seller's claim of agency and apply the Hanafi principle that one person's statement suffices in transactions.

Core Idea
In transactions, one credible informant's statement suffices; trustworthiness or predominant opinion determines permissibility.

This lesson explores a practical ruling from the Hanafi school: when you see someone selling a slave-girl that you know belongs to another, may you buy it based on the seller's claim of agency? The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies that the buyer may rely on the seller's statement if the seller is trustworthy (thiqah) or, if not, if the buyer's predominant opinion (ghālib al-ẓann) favors truthfulness. This is grounded in the necessity of facilitating transactions and the legal principle that predominant opinion stands in place of certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The buyer knows the slave-girl belongs to Khalid, but sees Zayd selling her and claiming agency from Khalid. The Hanafi ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) to buy and have intercourse with her under certain conditions.
The ruling is from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Understand the key evidentiary concepts
Two conditions are foundational: (1) the seller is thiqah (trustworthy), meaning his statements are reliable without further investigation; (2) if not thiqah, the buyer's ghālib al-ẓann (predominant opinion) must favor truthfulness. Both stem from the general principle that one person's statement is accepted in transactions.
Thiqah here does not require 'adālah (moral uprightness); sanity and general reliability suffice.
3
Analyze the proof (dalīl)
The proof is the general rule that in transactions, one credible informant's statement is accepted due to necessity (hājah). The commentator mentions that the informant's intellect and religion (implying honesty) support this. This is a rational proof (dalīl aqlī) based on removing hardship.
This differs from evidentiary requirements in other schools, which may require two witnesses.
4
Apply the exception when predominant opinion is of lying
If the buyer's predominant opinion is that the seller is lying, it is not permissible to proceed, because ghālib al-ẓann stands in place of certainty (yaqīn) in legal matters.
This shows that the ruling is not absolute but tied to the buyer's subjective assessment.
5
Consider the role of possession (yad)
The text also addresses a variant: if the buyer does not know the original owner, but the possessor claims ownership or agency, the same conditions apply. Additionally, if the buyer knows the original owner, he must not buy until transfer of ownership is known, because the original owner's possession (yad) is evidence of ownership.
Possession (yad) is prima facie evidence even for a fāsiq (sinner).

Source Text

He said: I bought it from him, or he gifted it to me, or he gave it in charity to me, based on what we said. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever knows a slave-girl that she belongs to a certain person, then sees another person selling her, and he says, 'The owner appointed me as agent to sell her,' then it is permissible for him to buy her and have intercourse with her, because he has given a true report that has no opposing evidence, and the statement of one person in transactions is accepted regardless of his description, due to the proof that has preceded. And similarly when he says, 'I bought her from him,' or 'he gifted her to me,' or 'he gave her in charity to me,' due to the same proof we have explained. Commentary: It has preceded that in transactions, the statement of one person is accepted; it is sufficient that the informant be sane, whether male or female, Muslim or disbeliever, upright or sinful. So when he sees Zayd selling a slave-girl in the market, and 'Umar knows that this slave-girl belongs to Khalid, but Zayd says that Khalid appointed him as agent to sell her, or says I bought her from Khalid, or says Khalid gifted her to me or gave her in charity to me, then in all these cases it is permissible for 'Umar to rely on Zayd's statement and buy the slave-girl and have intercourse with her, because this informant possesses intellect and religion in which lying is forbidden, so this report is true and has no opposing evidence, and this is a transaction in which the statement of one person is accepted. And this (acceptance of his statement) is when he is trustworthy, and similarly when he is not trustworthy but his predominant opinion is that he is truthful, because the integrity of the informant in transactions is not necessary due to necessity, as has preceded. And if his predominant opinion is that he is lying, it is not permissible for him to proceed with anything of that, because predominant opinion stands in place of certainty. And similarly when he does not know that this slave-girl belongs to so-and-so, but the possessor informs him that she belongs to so-and-so and that he appointed him as agent to sell her, or that he bought her from him, and the informant is trustworthy, his statement is accepted; and if he is not trustworthy, predominant opinion is considered, because his informing is evidence in his own right. And if the possessor does not inform him of anything, then if he knows that the slave-girl belongs to the first owner, he should not buy her until he learns of its transfer to the ownership of the second, because the possession of the first is evidence of his ownership; and if he does not know that, it is permissible for him to buy her even if the possessor is sinful, because the possession of a sinful person is evidence of ownership concerning the sinful and the upright, and there is no opposing evidence, and predominant opinion is not considered when there is clear evidence.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, commenting on Al-Hidayah, discusses the ruling on purchasing a known property (here a slave-girl) from a seller who claims agency or prior purchase from the owner. The Hanafi position, as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, is that it is permissible (ja'iz) for the buyer to rely on the seller's statement and proceed with the transaction, provided the seller is deemed trustworthy (thiqah) or, if not, the buyer's predominant opinion (ghālib al-ẓann) favors the seller's truthfulness. This leniency is based on necessity (hājah) in transactions, where requiring full verification would cause undue hardship. The commentator clarifies that the informant's 'adālah (moral integrity) is not a prerequisite; sanity alone suffices. If the buyer's predominant opinion is that the seller is lying, the transaction is not permissible, as predominant opinion is treated like certainty in legal matters. Additionally, if the buyer knows the previous owner, he must not purchase until he is certain the property has transferred to the seller's ownership, because possession (yad) is prima facie evidence of ownership. This ruling underscores that in Hanafi fiqh, practical necessity and predominant opinion often govern commercial transactions, balancing evidentiary rigor with real-world needs.

Key Terms
ثقہ (thiqah): A trustworthy informant whose truthfulness is reliably known; one whose statement is accepted without further investigation.
غالب گمان (ghālib al-ẓann): Predominant opinion or strong probability; a legal substitute for certainty in matters where certainty is unattainable.
ید (yad): Possession or control; physical custody of an item, which serves as prima facie evidence of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is never permissible.
B) It is permissible if the buyer's predominant opinion (ghālib al-ẓann) is that the seller is truthful.
C) It is permissible only if the seller provides a written contract.
D) It is permissible only if two witnesses confirm the seller's statement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, one person's statement suffices in transactions if the informant is trustworthy or if the buyer's predominant opinion favors truthfulness, due to necessity and the principle that predominant opinion stands in place of certainty.

Criterion of Harm in Hoarding: Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definition of harm in ihtikar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the definitions of harm (dharar) held by Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf in the context of ihtikar and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, only hoarding food harms the public; Abu Yusuf includes any commodity causing actual harm.

This short passage from the Hanafi tradition presents a nuanced internal debate on what constitutes harmful hoarding. Imam Abu Hanifa and his leading disciple Abu Yusuf disagree on the criterion of harm. Understanding this difference sharpens our ability to apply the prohibition of ihtikar across different commodities and reveals the depth of fiqh reasoning within a single school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is hoarding (ihtikar) of goods. The dispute is over which type of harm (dharar) makes hoarding reprehensible (makruh tahrimi).
The prohibition of ihtikar is well-established; the point of ikhtilaf is its scope.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his criterion
Imam Abu Hanifa (the 'Imam' in the passage) holds that only customary and conventional harm (dharar ma'hood wa muta'arif) matters, and that such harm is confined to foodstuffs because the body's constitution depends on food.
His reasoning is talil: the illah (cause) is customary harm, which is typically associated with food.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position and his criterion
Imam Abu Yusuf considers actual harm (dharar haqiqi) regardless of the commodity. Any hoarding that causes genuine hardship to the public is included.
He expands the scope beyond food to any essential item.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's view, hoarding non-food items (e.g., fuel, medicine) is not considered ihtikar even if it causes harm. Under Abu Yusuf's view, it would be prohibited if actual harm occurs.
This affects fatwa depending on which view is adopted as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدان کا قوام غذاء سے ہے کپڑوں سے نہیں۔ خلاصہ کلام امام ابو یوسف نے حقیقی ضرر کا اعتبار کیا ہے خواہ جس چیز میں ہو اور امام صاحب نے ضرر معہود و متعارف کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور ضر ر معهود و متعارف غذاؤں کے دکھنے میں ہے۔
The body's constitution is from food, not from clothes. Summary: Imam Abu Yusuf considered actual harm (haqiqi dharar) regardless of what it is in, while Imam [Abu Hanifa] considered customary and conventional harm (ma'hood wa muta'arif dharar), and customary and conventional harm is only in the case of food.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the definition of harm (dharar) that makes hoarding (ihtikar) reprehensible. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that any actual harm, in whatever commodity, is sufficient. Imam Abu Hanifa restricts harmful hoarding to foodstuffs because what is conventionally considered harmful to the public is only when food is withheld. This difference affects which goods can be subject to ihtikar.

Key Terms
ضرر (dharar): Harm that justifies prohibition of hoarding; disputed whether actual or customary
احتکار (ihtikar): Hoarding of foodstuffs to cause price rise
حقیقی ضرر (haqiqi dharar): Actual harm, regardless of customary perception
ضرر معہود و متعارف (dharar ma'hood wa muta'arif): Customary and conventional harm, recognized by common people

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The duration required for hoarding
B) Whether hoarding is ever permissible
C) The criterion of harm (dharar) that makes hoarding reprehensible
D) Whether hoarding one's own produce is allowed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the criterion of harm in ihtikar: customary (food only) vs actual (any commodity), with practical consequences for fatwa.

When a Hoarder Becomes Sinful: Intention and Conditions
Ruling on sin and conditions of ihtikar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a hoarder becomes sinful in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish between two levels of sin based on intention, and identify the conditions that make hoarding reprehensible.

Core Idea
The hoarder is sinful from the moment he withholds, regardless of duration; only worldly punishment depends on time.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a common confusion: whether the sin of hoarding depends on how long the grain is held. The answer is no—sin attaches immediately upon the intention to exploit others. However, the degree of sin varies: waiting for famine is worse than waiting for a normal price rise. The text also outlines the conditions that make hoarding legally reprehensible (makruh tahrimi) and notes that ordinary grain trade is praiseworthy if done honestly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ihtikar (hoarding) of foodstuffs. Determine its legal status (hukm) from the passage.
The passage states it is makruh tahrimi when conditions are met, and the hoarder is sinful.
2
Distinguish between sin and punishment
Note that the passage separates the concept of sin (gunah) from worldly punishment. The duration (40 days/month) is only for punishment, not for sin.
Sin is immediate upon hoarding with the intention to exploit.
3
Analyze the two levels of sin
The passage contrasts two intentions: waiting for price rise vs waiting for famine. Understand why the second is more sinful.
The second intends greater harm to the community.
4
Identify the conditions for ihtikar to be makruh
Extract the three conditions from the notes: harm to public, restriction to foodstuffs, and intention of hoarding.
If any condition is missing, the trade is not blameworthy.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Test your understanding: A person stocks grain intending to sell after a month at a fair profit. Is he sinful?
He is sinful because the intention is to wait for a price rise, even if short.

Source Text

When is the hoarder sinful? And the difference in sin occurs between waiting for high price and waiting for famine (may Allah protect us). And it is said that the duration is for punishment in this world; but the sin [occurs] even if the period is short. And the conclusion is that trade in grain is not praiseworthy. Muhammad Yusuf, may Allah forgive him. [Page 378] Ashraf al-Hidaya... Commentary: He who withholds grain intending to sell when prices rise, and he who withholds intending to sell when famine occurs to gain more profit, both are sinful, but the second is more sinful. And some scholars said that the duration is only for [the possibility of] punishment in this world; as for the sin, it is always present. The conclusion is that trade in grain is not praiseworthy. Note 1: This hoarding is only reprehensible when it is harmful to the public. (And this is the fatwa, as in Sabk al-Anhar p. 477 vol. 2) Note 2: According to both sides, hoarding is restricted to foodstuffs, and the fatwa is upon this. (Shami p. 255 vol. 5) Note 3: Trade in grain is not praiseworthy when the intention is hoarding; otherwise, it is praiseworthy because the trader is a friend of Allah.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage discusses the sinfulness of the hoarder (muhtakir). It distinguishes between two levels of sin: one who waits for normal price rise and one who waits for famine to cause maximum hardship; the latter is more sinful. A key point is that the duration (40 days or month) is relevant for worldly punishment but not for sin; the hoarder is sinful from the moment he withholds with bad intention, even if the period is short. Three important notes follow: (1) ihtikar is only reprehensible when it harms the public; (2) it is restricted to foodstuffs (aqwat); (3) trade in grain itself is not blameworthy if the intention is not hoarding—in fact, a trader is considered a friend of Allah if he deals honestly.

Key Terms
گناہگار (gunahgar): Sinful person; the hoarder is sinful regardless of duration
مضر (mudirr): Harmful; ihtikar is only reprehensible when harmful to the public
احتکار (ihtikar): Hoarding; the act of withholding goods to exploit price rise

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
A hoarder becomes sinful immediately upon hoarding with bad intention, but the act is only makruh tahrimi if it harms the public and involves foodstuffs.

Procedure for Dealing with a Hoarder
Explains the qadi's initial and subsequent actions against a hoarder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two-step procedure a qadi follows when a complaint of hoarding (ihtikar) is made, and explain the rationale for the graduated response.

Core Idea
The qadi first warns the hoarder to sell surplus; only on repetition does he imprison and punish.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi fiqh on how a qadi should handle complaints of hoarding (ihtikar). You will see that Islamic jurisprudence balances public welfare with individual correction, providing a graduated response that avoids immediate harshness. The passage highlights the importance of first giving the offender a chance to rectify, and only escalating when necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
Recognize that ihtikar (hoarding essential goods) is prohibited in Hanafi fiqh as makruh tahrimi. This sets the context for state intervention.
Hoarding means withholding food or necessities to drive up prices and cause public harm.
2
Outline the initial qadi response
Upon receiving a verified complaint, the qadi orders the hoarder to sell the surplus beyond his family's needs. This is a warning and a command to desist.
The qadi does not punish immediately; he gives an opportunity to comply.
3
Understand the escalation condition
If the same complaint is brought again (i.e., the hoarder repeats the offense), the qadi escalates by imprisoning the hoarder and administering ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
Ta'zir can include beating or other measures as the qadi deems appropriate.
4
Analyze the rationale
The graduated approach aims to first correct with minimal intervention, but if public harm persists, stronger measures are justified. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on social welfare and proportionate response.
The ultimate goal is removal of harm (darar) from the people.

كتاب الكراهية
ترجمہ اور جب قاضی کی جانب یہ معاملہ اٹھایا گیا ( یعنی اس تک یہ شکایت پہنچائی گئی کہ فلاں احتکار کرتا ہے ) تو قاضی محتمر کو حکم کرے کہ اتنے غلہ کے بیچنے کا جو اس کی روزی سے اور اس کے اہل و عیال کی روزی سے زیادہ ہو اس سلسلہ میں فراغت کے اعتبار سے اور اس کو احتکار سے روک دے پس اگر یہ معاملہ دوبارہ لے جایا گیا (یعنی دوبارہ پھر اس کی یہی شکایت موصول ہوئی ) تو قاضی اس کو قید میں ڈال دے اور اس کی تعزیر کرے جتنی مناسب سمجھے اس کو جر کرتے ہوئے اور لوگوں کے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے۔ تشریح قاضی کو بتایا گیا کہ فلاں شخص احتکار کرتا ہے تو قاضی اس کو سمجھادے اور کہ دے کہ جتنا فراغت کے ساتھ تیرے اور تیرے اہل وعیال کیلئے کافی ہو اتنا روک لے اور باقی کو فروخت کر دے لیکن اگر وہ باز نہ آئے اور دوبارہ قاضی کے پاس پھر یہی شکایت پہنچی تو قاضی اس کو گرفتار کرے اور قید خانہ میں ڈال دے اور جتنی مناسب سمجھے اتنی اس کی پٹائی کرے تا کہ اس کو زجر ہو اور لوگوں سے ضر ر دور ہو۔
Translation: And when this matter is brought to the qadi (i.e., the complaint reaches him that so-and-so is hoarding), then the qadi orders the hoarder to sell from the grain that exceeds his own sustenance and that of his family, in terms of having ease, and prevents him from hoarding. Then if the matter is brought again (i.e., the same complaint is received again), then the qadi imprisons him and gives him ta'zeer as he deems appropriate, chastising him and for the removal of harm from the people. Commentary: It is said to the qadi that so-and-so is hoarding, so the qadi advises him and says: keep enough for your and your family's ease and sell the rest. But if he does not desist and the same complaint reaches the qadi again, then the qadi arrests him and puts him in prison and beats him as appropriate so that he is deterred and harm is removed from the people.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on disliked matters (Kitab al-Karahiyah). It outlines the legal procedure when a complaint of hoarding (ihtikar) is made to the qadi. The Hanafi ruling is that initially the hoarder is given a chance to voluntarily sell the surplus above his family's needs. If he repeats the offense, the qadi is authorized to imprison him and administer a discretionary punishment (ta'zeer) to prevent public harm. This demonstrates that hoarding essential commodities is prohibited and the state has the authority to intervene to protect the community.

Key Terms
احتکار (ihtikar): Hoarding food or essential goods to cause price rise and harm the public.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the qadi, not fixed by Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qadi follows a graduated procedure: first warn and order sale of surplus; only on repeat does he resort to imprisonment and ta'zir to deter hoarding and protect public welfare.

Conditions for Permissibility of Price Fixing (Tas'ir) in Hanafi Fiqh
States the conditions under which price fixing becomes permissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that make price fixing permissible for the qadi and apply them to a real scenario.

Core Idea
Price fixing is allowed only when merchants overprice excessively, the qadi has no other recourse, and he consults experts.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary explains the ruling on price fixing (tas'ir). While the school generally discourages market intervention, it recognizes a necessity when public harm is severe. The qadi must assess the situation and act only with expert advice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Determine what 'tas'ir' (price fixing) is and note that the Hanafi default is dislike (karahah) due to interference with free market. However, this passage addresses when it becomes permissible.
The default ruling is makruh, but necessity can override.
2
List the conditions that override the default
From the text, extract the specific conditions: (1) merchants are oppressive and overprice excessively (ta'addin fahish), (2) the qadi cannot protect Muslims' rights except by fixing prices, and (3) the qadi consults with people of opinion and insight (ahl al-ray wa al-basira).
All three must be present.
3
Explain the role of consultation
The qadi must consult knowledgeable market experts to set a fair price that prevents harm to both parties. This ensures the price is just and not arbitrary.
Consultation is a condition for validity, not just recommended.
4
Apply to a hypothetical case
Consider a scenario: grain merchants double prices due to a cartel, causing hardship. The qadi is unable to stop the oppression without price controls. After consulting experienced traders, he sets a maximum price. Check if all conditions are met.
This scenario matches the conditions, so tas'ir is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کب بھاؤ مقرر کر سکتا ہے
فان كان ارباب الطعام يتحكمون ويتعدون عن القيمة تعديا فاحشا وعجز القاضي عن صيانة حقوق المسلمين الا بالتسعيــر فـحـيـنـتـذ لا بأس به بمشورة من اهل الراى والبصيرة ترجمہ. پس اگر ہوں غلہ والے تحکم کرتے ہوں اور تجاوز کرتے ہوں قیمت سے تجاوز فاحش اور قاضی عاجز ہو جائے مسلمانوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت سے مگر بھاؤ مقرر کرنے کے ساتھ ، تو اس وقت بھاؤ مقرر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں اہل رائے اور اہل بصیرت کے
مشورہ سے۔
تشریح جولوگ غلہ فروش ہیں جیسے ہمارے یہاں پیسے جو لوگوں پر ظلم و ستم کرنے پر کمر بستہ ہیں اور بغیر کنٹرول ریٹ کے لوگوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت مشکل ہے تو اس وقت کنٹرول ریٹ مقرر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں بلکہ قاضی ایسا کر دے تا کہ لوگ ظلم وستم سے محفوظ رہ سکیں لیکن قاضی کو چاہئے کہ ہر زمانہ میں باشعور لوگوں سے مشورہ کرے کہ کیا ریٹ مقرر کیا جائے جن کو غلہ کے معاملہ میں تجربہ اور شعور ہوتا که فریقین نقصان اور خسارہ سے محفوظ رہ سکیں۔
When can the qadi fix prices? For if the food merchants are oppressive and exceed the value excessively, and the qadi is unable to safeguard the rights of Muslims except by price fixing, then at that time there is no harm in it, with the consultation of people of opinion and insight. Translation: So if the grain dealers are oppressive and transgress from the price excessively, and the qadi becomes helpless in protecting the rights of Muslims except by fixing the price, then at that time there is no harm in fixing the price with the consultation of people of opinion and insight. Commentary: Those who are grain sellers, like in our times who are bent on oppressing people, and without a controlled rate it is difficult to protect people's rights, then at that time there is no harm in fixing a controlled rate, rather the qadi should do so so that people can be safe from oppression and tyranny. But the qadi should consult wise people every time as to what price should be fixed, who have experience and knowledge in grain matters so that both parties can be safe from loss and damage.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on price fixing (tas'ir) in the Hanafi school. Generally, price fixing is disliked (makruh) because it restricts free market. However, when merchants engage in excessive overpricing (ta'addin fahish) and the qadi has no other means to protect public rights, price fixing becomes permissible. The qadi must consult with knowledgeable and experienced people (ahl al-ray wa al-basira) to set a fair price that prevents harm to both buyers and sellers. This ruling is based on the principle of preventing public harm (darar 'amm).

Key Terms
تسعیر (tas'ir): The act of fixing a maximum price for goods by the state or qadi.
تعدی فاحش (ta'addin fahish): Excessive transgression in pricing, typically doubling the normal price as per commentary.
اهل الراى والبصيرة (ahl al-ray wa al-basira): People of opinion and insight; knowledgeable experts in the relevant market.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition makes price fixing permissible for the qadi?
A) Any merchant disagreement
B) Excessive price increase and inability to protect rights otherwise
C) Majority of merchants agree
D) The ruler's whim

Key Takeaway
Price fixing in Hanafi law is a restricted emergency measure requiring three conditions: excessive overpricing, necessity, and expert consultation.

Selling Above Fixed Price and the Qadi's Authority Over Hoarder's Goods
Rules on selling above fixed price and intra-Hanafi dispute on selling hoarder's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a sale above a fixed price is valid and analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a qadi can sell a hoarder's property without consent.

Core Idea
Sales above fixed price are valid; qadi may sell hoarder's goods by consensus for public harm.

This lesson examines two interrelated issues from the chapter on price control (tas'ir). First, we explore the Hanafi consensus that a sale exceeding the qadi's fixed price remains valid due to the absence of coercion. Second, we delve into an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the qadi may forcibly sell a hoarder's grain to prevent public harm. The analysis reveals how the principle of hajr (legal restriction) and the concept of 'general harm' shape the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct but connected cases: (1) selling above a qadi's fixed price, and (2) selling a hoarder's grain without his consent. Note that the first case enjoys consensus, while the second involves ikhtilaf.
The second case builds on the first by raising the question of coercion.
2
State the Hanafi position on the first case
All three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree: if someone sells above the fixed price, the qadi validates the sale. Abu Hanifa argues no hajr on a free person; the Sahibayn add that hajr only applies to a specified group, which is absent here.
The key is that the seller chose to sell voluntarily; he was only compelled to sell at a certain price if he sold, not to sell itself.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the second case
Two views are reported. The first: it follows the known disagreement on selling a debtor's property (Abu Hanifa forbids, Sahibayn permit). The second: by consensus, the qadi may sell because Abu Hanifa himself allows hajr to repel general harm, and hoarding causes such harm.
This second view is supported by a note from Sakb al-Anhar stating 'by consensus'.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each opinion
The first opinion hinges on whether hajr is permissible on a free person. The second opinion uses qiyas: just as the qadi can ban an ignorant physician to prevent harm, he can sell the hoarder's goods. This is what Abu Hanifa would say, so the ikhtilaf is resolved.
The commentary suggests the second view is stronger and mufta bihi.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the first view is taken, the qadi cannot force the sale unless the hoarder is a debtor (Sahibayn view). Under the second view, the qadi can always sell to prevent public harm. The notes also clarify that in times of oppression, price fixing becomes wajib.
The lesson demonstrates how usul principles (hajr, ikrah) apply to market regulation.

Source Text

- قاضی نے جو ریٹ مقرر کیا ہے اگر کسی نے بدمعاشی کی اور اس نے زیادہ بھاؤ میں بیچا تو کیا حکم ہے تو جواب دیا کا بالاتفاق یہ بیج جائز ہوگی اور قاضی اس بیع کو نہ توڑے، کیوں؟ اسلئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک تو آزاد پر حجر ہی جائز نہیں تو وہ مجبور نہیں ہوا بلکہ خود مختار ہے اور مختار کا تصرف جائز ہی ہوا کرتا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک اگر چہ حجر جائز ہے لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ جن پر حجر عائد ہو وہ مجہول نہ ہوں بلکہ معین ہوں اور یہاں معین نہیں بلکہ مجہول ہیں اسلئے یہ حجر نہیں تو یہ مجبور نہیں ہوا بلکہ مختار ہے تو اس کا تصرف نافذ ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر اناج بیچنے والی کوئی معین قوم ہو تو ان پر تجر صاحبین کے نزدیک نائز ہوگا ، درست ہوگا ۔ پھر ان کی بیع اس ریٹ سے زیادہ کے ساتھ جو قاضی نے مقرر کیا ہے جائز نہ ہوگی۔ قاضی نے جو ریٹ مقرر کر دیا ہے اگر کوئی اسی ریٹ پر فروخت کرے تو بیع جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو بیچنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا گیا ہے بلکہ مجبور اس پر کیا گیا ہے کہ جب بیچے تو اس ریٹ پر بیچے تو یہ بیچ پر اکراہ نہیں ہے اسلئے بیع جائز ہے۔ -۳- جب مختصر اپنا غلہ بیچنے سے انکار کمرے تو کیا قاضی اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر اس کا غلہ فروخت کر سکتا ہے تو ایک قول کے مطابق اس میں اختلاف ہے یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نہیں بیچ سکتا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بیچ سکتا ہے اور یہ اختلاف ایسا ہے جیسے کوئی مدیون ہو اور اس کے ذمہ دوسروں کا قرض ہو اور اسکے پاس مال ہے جس کو بیچ کر وہ اپنا قرض ادا کر سکتا ہے لیکن وہ اپنا مال بیچ کر قرض ادا نہیں کرتا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک قاضی مدیون کا مال نہیں نیچے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بیچ دے گا تو یہی اختلاف یہاں پر بھی ہے۔ اور دوسرا قول یہاں پر یہ ہے کہ قاضی بالاتفاق ایسے منکر کا غلہ اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر فروخت کر سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ امام صاحب ضرر عام کو دور کرنے کیلئے حجر کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں اور یہاں جو حجر ہے اس میں بھی ضرر عام کو دور کرنا ہے۔ جیسے قاضی کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ جاہل
طبیب اور ڈاکٹر پر پابندی عائد کر دے تا کہ ضر ر عام دور ہو سکے۔
تنبیہ - بغیر ضرورت کے بھاؤ مقرر کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ (شامی ص ۲۵۶ ج ۵)
تنبیه ۲ تجاوز فاحش سے مراد یہ ہے کہ دوگنی قیمت پر فروخت کریں۔ (شامی ص ۲۵۶ ج ۵)
تنبیه - بوقت ظلم و ستم قاضی پر ریٹ مقرر کرنا واجب ہے۔ (شامی ص ۲۵۶ ج ۵) و
اگر مختمر بیع نہ کرے تو قاضی بالا تفاقی اس کے غلہ کوفروخت کر دے۔ سكب الانه ر ص ۴۷۷ ج ۲)
What is the ruling for one who disobeys the qadi? For if he does that (fixes a price) and a man exceeds it and sells for more than it, the qadi validates the sale. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa because he does not permit restriction (hajr) on a free person; and likewise according to them [Sahibayn] unless the restriction is on a specific group, and whoever among them sells at the price set by the imam, the sale is valid because he is not compelled to sell. And can the qadi sell the hoarder's food without his consent? It is said that it is upon the difference known in selling the property of a debtor. And it is said that he sells by consensus because Abu Hanifa permits restriction for repelling general harm, and this is similar. Translation: So if the qadi did that (fixed a controlled rate) and a person exceeded it and sold for more, the qadi will validate the sale (i.e., not break it). This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa because he does not consider restriction on a free person valid, and similarly according to the Sahibayn unless the restriction is on a specific group, and whoever among them sold at the price set by the imam, it is valid because he was not compelled to sell. And can the qadi sell the hoarder's grain without his consent? It is said that this is on the difference known in selling the property of a debtor, and it is said that he sells by consensus because Abu Hanifa considers restriction permissible for repelling general harm, and this is similar. Commentary: In this passage three issues are mentioned. (1) If someone mischievously sold at a higher price than the rate set by the qadi, what is the ruling? The answer is that by consensus this sale will be valid and the qadi will not break it, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa restriction on a free person is not valid, so he was not coerced but was free, and a free person's disposition is valid. According to the Sahibayn, although restriction is valid, the condition is that those restricted must be specified, not unknown; here they are unknown, so there is no restriction, so he was not coerced, so his disposition is effective. However, if there is a specific group of grain sellers, then restriction on them according to the Sahibayn is valid, and their sale at a higher price than the qadi's fixed rate will not be valid. If someone sells at the fixed price, the sale is valid because he was not forced to sell; he was only forced if he sells to sell at that price, so this is not compulsion (ikrah), hence sale is valid. (3) When the hoarder refuses to sell his grain, can the qadi sell his grain without his consent? According to one view, there is difference: Imam Abu Hanifa says he cannot sell, while the Sahibayn say he can. This difference is like the case of a debtor who has property but refuses to sell it to pay debts; Abu Hanifa says the qadi does not sell his property, while the Sahibayn say he does. According to another view, the qadi can sell by consensus because Imam Abu Hanifa allows restriction to repel general harm, and this is similar to that, like the qadi may ban an ignorant physician to prevent general harm. Note: Fixing price without necessity is makruh. (Shami vol.5 p.256). Note2: 'excessive transgression' means selling at double the price. (Shami vol.5 p.256). Note: In times of oppression, fixing price is wajib upon the qadi. (Shami vol.5 p.256). And if the hoarder does not sell, the qadi sells his grain by consensus. (Sakb al-Anhar vol.2 p.477).
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage covers three interrelated issues after the qadi fixes a price. First, if someone sells above the fixed price, the sale is valid by consensus of all Hanafi imams. According to Abu Hanifa, no restriction (hajr) can be placed on a free person, so the seller acted voluntarily. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, restriction is possible only on a specified group, and here the public is unspecified, so again no coercion. Second, if the price fix is applied to a specific group, then selling above the fixed price is invalid according to the Sahibayn. Third, can the qadi sell the hoarder's grain without his consent? There are two views: one follows the disagreement over selling a debtor's property (Abu Hanifa forbids, Sahibayn permit); the other view says by consensus the qadi may sell because preventing public harm justifies restriction—Abu Hanifa himself allows restriction for general harm. The notes add that price fixing without necessity is makruh, that 'excessive transgression' means doubling the price, that in times of oppression price fixing becomes wajib on the qadi, and that if the hoarder refuses, the qadi can sell his grain by consensus.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Legal restriction on a person's ability to dispose of his property.
مدیون (madyun): A debtor who has property but refuses to sell it to pay debts.
اکراہ (ikrah): Compulsion that invalidates free consent in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a sale made at a price higher than the qadi's fixed price?
A) The sale is invalid and the qadi breaks it
B) The sale is valid and the qadi does not break it
C) The seller is punished but the sale stands
D) The buyer must pay the difference

Key Takeaway
A sale above a qadi's fixed price is valid because the seller acts voluntarily; the qadi may sell a hoarder's goods by consensus to prevent public harm.
