Restriction of Churches and Wine to Villages: An Intra-Hanafi Refinement
Intra-Hanafi refinement of a ruling on dhimmi practices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school restricts the permission for churches and wine to villages and evaluate how later scholars refined the ruling.

Core Idea
The exception for sawad was specific to Sawad al-Kufa; where Islam dominates, villages equal cities.

This passage addresses a crucial intra-Hanafi refinement. The original text from Imam Muhammad permitted dhimmis to build churches and sell wine in villages (sawad) but not in cities, due to the dominance of Islamic symbols in cities. However, later shuyukh clarified that this permission was temporal and geographical—specific to Sawad al-Kufa where most inhabitants were dhimmis. Wherever Islam is dominant, the ruling is the same as cities: such activities are prohibited. This lesson traces this legal evolution.

Guided Path
1
State the Original Ruling
Identify the matn's position: dhimmis may build churches and sell wine in villages (sawad) but are prevented in cities (amsar).
The matn is from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Identify the Reason for the Restriction to Cities
The reason is the manifestation of Islamic symbols (shi'ar al-Islam) in cities; symbols of disbelief cannot be public where Islam is dominant.
This is the core principle: dominance of Islamic symbols overrides permission.
3
Understand the Rationale of the Exception for Sawad
The exception for sawad was based on the fact that Sawad al-Kufa was predominantly dhimmi, so Islamic symbols were not dominant there.
This exception was not a general rule but a contextual one.
4
Recognize the Refinement by Later Shuyukh
Later scholars (shuyukh) restricted the exception to Sawad al-Kufa. In other villages where Islam is dominant, the same prohibition as cities applies.
This refinement is described as 'al-ashahh' (the most correct view).
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The relied-upon position is that dhimmis are not permitted to build churches or publicly sell wine in any area where Islamic symbols dominate, whether city or village.
This is the operative view for fatwa.

Source Text

تنبیه یہ بحث ہدایہ ج ۲ ص ۵۷۷ پر گذر چکی ہے۔
And he restricted it to the countryside because they (the dhimmis) are not permitted to take churches and convents and to display the sale of wines and pigs in the cities, due to the manifestation of Islamic symbols therein, contrary to the countryside. They (the shuyukh) said: This was in the Sawad of Kufa, because most of its inhabitants were dhimmis. As for our Sawad, the symbols of Islam are manifest therein, so they will not be permitted there either, and this is the most correct. The shuyukh said: This was in the villages of Kufa because most of its inhabitants were dhimmis. As for our villages, the symbols of Islam are manifest, so the dhimmis will not be given power in those villages either, and this is the most correct. Commentary: The text stated that if these matters occur in a village there is no harm. Why was the restriction to villages made? It was made because Islamic symbols are prevalent and dominant in cities, so symbols of disbelief will not be permitted in cities. But this was about the villages of Kufa at that time, whose inhabitants were mostly dhimmis. In other regions besides Kufa, cities and villages are equal in this regard because Islamic symbols are common in both cities and villages. Note: This discussion has passed in Hidayah vol. 2 p. 577.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the restriction of dhimmis building churches and selling wine/pigs to villages. The matn (from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir) states that dhimmis are prevented from doing these things in cities (amsar) due to the dominance of Islamic symbols, but they are allowed in villages (sawad). However, later shuyukh (scholars) clarified that this ruling was specific to Sawad al-Kufa, where the majority were dhimmis. In other villages where Islam is dominant, the ruling is the same as cities—they are not permitted. This is the relied-upon position (al-ashahh). The commentary expands that the restriction originally gave an exception for villages in Kufa, but that exception does not apply generally. The author follows the order: first states the ruling, then gives the reason, then presents the later refinement, and confirms the more correct view.

Key Terms
السواد (al-sawad): The rural countryside or villages, as opposed to amsar (cities).
شعائر الإسلام (shi'ar al-Islam): The visible symbols and practices of Islam that are dominant in a locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because villages are not cities.
B) No, because Islamic symbols are dominant there just like in cities.
C) Yes, as long as they are in Sawad al-Kufa.
D) No, only in cities.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling permits dhimmis to build churches and sell wine only where Islamic symbols are not dominant; the historical permission for Sawad al-Kufa is not a general rule.

The Changing Ruling on Quranic Markings: Ta'shir and Nuqt
Ruling on ta'shir and nuqt in the Quran and its change over time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on ta'shir and nuqt, identify the dalil from Ibn Mas'ud, and explain why the ruling changed to mustahsan for non-Arabs.

Core Idea
A practice originally makruh can become mustahsan when necessity arises — rulings change with time and circumstance.

Marking every ten verses and adding vowel dots to the Quran are common features of modern Quranic prints. Yet the early Hanafi school considered them makruh, based on a companion's instruction. This lesson explores the reasoning behind that original ruling and its later transformation into a recommended practice for non-Arabs, illustrating a key Hanafi principle that necessity can override a disliked ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
The act is ta'shir (marking tens) and nuqt (vowel dots) in the mushaf. The original ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is makruh (disliked).
The ruling is found in Kitab al-Karahiyyah of al-Hidayah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Jarridu al-Qur'an' (Keep the Quran pure), which implies not adding any extraneous markings.
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a non-definitive proof in Hanafi usul (zanni al-thubut).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'tajrid' means to keep the Quran free from non-Quranic additions. Markings distract from memorizing the text and i'rab, so they contradict tajrid.
The reliance on written aids may weaken one's ability to recite without them.
4
Recognize the change by later scholars
The mashayikh ruled that for non-Arabs ('Ajam), these markings are necessary to prevent the abandonment of Quran recitation. Thus, it becomes hasan (mustahsan) for them.
This change is based on istihsan (juristic preference) due to necessity.
5
Apply the principle of taghayyur al-fatwa
The passage explicitly notes that rulings change with time and place (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman wa al-makan).
This is a recognized maxim in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسائل متفرقه
ترجمہ: یہ متفرق مسائل ہیں
تشریح: اس عنوان کے تحت مختلف الانواع مسائل کو جمع کیا جاتا ہے۔
قرآن میں تعشیر اور نقطے لگانے کا حکم
كتاب الكراهية
قال ويكره التعشير والنقط فى المصحف لقول ابن مسعود رضى الله عنه جردوا القرآن ويروى جردها . المصاحف وفي التعشير والنقط ترك التجريد ولان التعشير يخل بحفظ الاى والنقط بحفظ الاعراب اتكالا عليه فيكره قالوا في زماننا لابد للعجم من دلالة فترك ذلك اخلال بالحفظ وهجران القرآن فيكون حسنا
ترجمہ: محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور تعشیر ( دہائی پر علامت لگانا ) اور قرآن میں نقطے لگانا مکروہ ہے ابن مسعود کے قول کی وجہ سے قرآن کی دوسری چیزوں سے خالی کرو اور روایت کیا گیا ہے مصاحف کو دوسری چیزوں سے خالی کرو اور تعشیر اور نقطے لگانے میں تجرید کو چھوڑنا ہے اور اسلئے کہ تعشیر حفظ آیات میں مخل ہے اور نقطے لگانا حفظ اعراب میں مخل ہے اس پر اعتماد کرنے کی وجہ سے تو یہ مکروہ ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ ہمارے زمانے میں عجم کیلئے کسی علامات و دلالت کا ہونا ضروری ہے تو اس کا چھوڑ نا حفظ میں مخل ہے اور قرآن کو چھوڑنا ہے۔ تو یہ حسن ہوگا۔
تشریح: تعشیر“ ہر دس آیت پر نشان لگانا ، نقطہ نقطے لگانا، ” تجرید خالی کرنا ، یعنی غیر قرآن کو نہ لکھا جائے ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں حکم دیا گیا ہے کہ قرآن کو غیر قرآن سے خالی کرواسی وجہ سے آمین بھی نہیں لکھا جاتا تو قرآن پر نقطے اور اعراب لگانا اسی طرح ہر دس آیت کے بعد نشان لگانا اور جیسے رکوع مقرر کرنا سب مکروہ ہے کیونکہ تجرید کے منافی ہے نیز تعشیر اور نقط آیات کو یاد کرنے میں مخل ہوں گے اور اعراب کو یاد کرنے میں مخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ سب لوگ لکھے ہوئے پر اعتماد کر کے یاد کرنا چھوڑ دیں کے لیکن مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ ہمارے زمانہ میں عجمیوں کیلئے اعراب کا اور نقط کا ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ اس کے بغیر نہیں پڑھ سکیں گے تو ان کے حق میں اعراب وغیرہ کا ہونا ضروی ہے ورنہ وہ بالکل قرآن کو چھوڑ بیٹھیں گے۔ اسی وجہ سے اعراب وغیرہ مستحسن ہے۔
خلاصہ کلام یہ بدعت حسنہ ہے۔
تنبیہ: اور ممانعت نزول قرآن کے زمانہ تک مخصوص ہے نیز ان کیلئے بغیر اعراب کے پڑھنا سہل تھا تو ان کے حق میں تعشیر و نقط حفظ آیات اور حفظ اعراب میں منخل تھا اور ہمارے زمانے میں یہ بات نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ مستحسن ہے اور زمان ومکان کے اختلاف سے احکام میں اختلاف ہو جاتا ہے۔ کذا في مجمع الانهر ص ۵۳۰ ج ۲ و البسط فی الشامی ص ۲۴۷ ج ۵
Miscellaneous issues. Explanation: Under this heading various types of issues are collected. Ruling on ta'shir and nuqt in the Quran. In Kitab al-Karahiyyah, it is said: It is makruh to put tens markers and dots in the mus'haf due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Keep the Quran pure (from other things).' It is also narrated to keep the mus'hafs pure. In ta'shir and nuqt, there is abandonment of purity. Also, ta'shir interferes with memorizing verses, and nuqt interferes with memorizing i'rab, because one relies on them, so it is makruh. The scholars said: In our time, non-Arabs need guidance; abandoning it would harm memorization and lead to abandoning the Quran, so it is good. Explanation: Ta'shir means marking every ten verses; nuqt means putting vowel points; tajrid means keeping free from non-Quran. The meaning is that the hadith commands to keep the Quran free from non-Quran, so writing ameen is not done. Placing dots and i'rab, as well as marking tens, is makruh because it contradicts tajrid. However, the latter scholars said that in our time, for non-Arabs, i'rab and dots are necessary; otherwise they cannot read, so it is mustahsan. Summary: It is a good innovation. Note: The prohibition was specific to the time of revelation, when reading without i'rab was easy. Now it is mustahsan. Rulings change with time and place.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on adding markers for every ten verses (ta'shir) and vowel dots (nuqt) in the Quran. The matn states it is makruh, citing Ibn Mas'ud's instruction to keep the Quran free from extraneous markings. The reasoning is that such markings distract from memorization and reliance on them may weaken one's ability to recite without aids. However, the later scholars (mashayikh) ruled that for non-Arabs ('Ajam), these markings are necessary; without them, they would abandon the Quran entirely. Therefore, in their case, it is considered hasan (good) and a 'good innovation' (bid'ah hasanah). The passage emphasizes that rulings can change with time and place (taghayyur al-fatawa bi taghayyur al-azman). This is a clear example of the Hanafi principle that necessity can override a disliked ruling.

Key Terms
تعشیر (ta'shīr): Marking every ten verses of the Quran.
نقط (nuqṭ): Vowel dots and i'rab markings in the Quran.
تجرید (tajrīd): Keeping the Quran free from non-Quranic additions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Makruh (disliked)
B) Haram (forbidden)
C) Mustahsan (recommended)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ta'shir and nuqt changed from makruh to mustahsan for non-Arabs due to necessity (istihsan), demonstrating that rulings can change with time, place, and circumstance.

Ruling on Ta'shir and Nuqat in the Mushaf
Ruling on ta'shir and nuqat with proof from Ibn Mas'ud and later revision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'shir and nuqat in the Quran, identify the primary evidence from Ibn Mas'ud, and explain why later scholars changed the ruling to hasan for non-Arabs.

Core Idea
Placing markers in the Quran was initially makruh, but later became commendable for non-Arabs to prevent neglect.

This lesson examines a fascinating case in Hanafi fiqh where a ruling changes over time due to necessity. The passage addresses the permissibility of adding verse markers (ta'shir) and diacritical dots (nuqat) to the Quran. While early scholars considered this makruh following Ibn Mas'ud's instruction to keep the mushaf bare, later Hanafi authorities recognized that for non-Arab Muslims, such aids are essential to preserve correct recitation. This demonstrates the principle of istihsan and the evolution of rulings based on changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The passage first states that ta'shir and nuqat are makruh. This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
The act is placing verse markers and diacritical dots in the Quran.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'جردوا القرآن' (strip the Quran bare). This is a qawl sahabi, considered hujja in the Hanafi school.
The evidence is transmitted, but its transmission is zanni.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'jard' (strip) indicates that the Quran should be free of extraneous marks. Adding marks would contradict this instruction, hence the karahah.
The imperative form (amr) here implies prohibition or dislike.
4
Note the change due to necessity
Later scholars ('mashayikh') considered that for non-Arabs ('ajam), abandoning these marks would lead to neglect of the Quran. So they shifted the ruling to hasan (recommendable).
This change is based on istihsan, overriding the original evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The later ruling (mufta bihi) is that these markings are commendable for non-Arabs due to necessity. This is an example of istihsan overriding the original zahir.
The authority for the change comes from the later mashayikh (muta'akhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويكره التعشير والنقط فى المصحف لقول ابن مسعود رضى الله عنه جردوا القرآن ويروى جردوا المصاحف وفي التعشير والنقط ترك التجريد ولان التعشير يخل بحفظ الآي والنقط بحفظ الاعراب اتكالا عليه فيكره قالوا في زماننا لابد للعجم من دلالة فترك ذلك اخلال بالحفظ وهجران القرآن فيكون حسنا
He said: And it is disliked (makruh) to place verse markers (ta'shir) and dots (nuqat) in the mushaf because of the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Strip the Quran bare' and it is narrated: 'Strip the musahif bare.' And in placing verse markers and dots there is abandonment of stripping bare, and because verse markers interfere with memorizing the verses, and dots interfere with memorizing the grammatical endings, relying on them, so it is disliked. They said: In our time, non-Arabs necessarily need indication, so abandoning that would be harmful to memorization and abandonment of the Quran, so it becomes good (hasan).
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on adding punctuation and verse markers to the Quran. Initially, the practice is considered makruh (disliked) based on the instruction of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud to keep the Quran free from extra markings. The ruling is motivated by the concern that such aids would lead people to rely on written cues rather than memorizing the text and its correct recitation. However, later scholars (mashayikh) recognized that for non-Arab Muslims, these marks are essential to prevent complete neglect of Quranic reading. Therefore, in our time, the ruling shifts to hasan (recommendable) to facilitate proper recitation. This exemplifies a ruling that changes with time and circumstance within the Hanafi school, being an instance of istihsan based on necessity.

Key Terms
التعشير (al-ta'shir): Placing marks at every ten verses in the Quran.
النقط (al-nuqt): Dots placed on letters to distinguish them (diacritization).
التجريد (al-tajrid): Keeping the Quran free of any extraneous markings or text.
العجم (al-'ajam): Non-Arabs, particularly Persians, who need linguistic aids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why did the Hanafi scholars later consider placing dots and verse markers in the Quran as hasan (good) rather than makruh?
A) Because it is an innovation.
B) Because non-Arabs needed the marks to read correctly.
C) Because Ibn Mas'ud commanded it.
D) Because it makes the Quran beautiful.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the ruling on ta'shir and nuqat to shift from makruh to hasan for non-Arabs based on necessity, illustrating the principle of istihsan.

Ruling on Adorning the Quran with Gold (Tahliyat al-Masahif)
Ruling with qiyas proof on adorning the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adorning the Quran with gold and explain the qiyas proof used, identifying the illa of veneration.

Core Idea
Adorning the Quran with gold is permissible (la ba's) because it shows veneration, analogised to decorating mosques.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on adorning the Quran with gold. While some may view this as extravagance, the Hanafi school permits it based on a clear analogy to mosque decoration. Let's explore the proof from al-Quduri's matn and its expansion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahliyat al-masahif (adorning the Quran with gold). The ruling stated is 'la ba's' (no harm), which in Hanafi fiqh means permissible (mubah).
The Arabic phrase 'la ba's' is a common expression for permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is a qiyas (analogy): adorning the Quran is compared to decorating the mosque with gold water, which is also permissible.
The text says 'صار كنقش المسجد وتزيينه بماء الذهب' – it has become like engraving and decorating the mosque with gold water.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) binding the two cases is veneration (ta'dhim). Just as decorating a mosque is a form of respect, adorning the Quran similarly shows veneration.
The illa is explicitly stated in 'لما فيه من تعظيمه' – because of the veneration it contains.
4
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that it is permissible (mubah). However, the intention must be sincere ta'dhim, not pride or waste. If done with mosque funds, the trustee may become liable.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah through Quduri's matn, and is upheld in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا بأس بتحلية المصاحف لما فيه من تعظيمه وصار كنقش المسجد وتزيينه بماء الذهب وقد ذكرناه من قبل
He said: There is no harm in adorning the musahif because of the veneration it contains, and it has become like engraving the mosque and decorating it with gold water, and we have mentioned it before.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling that adorning the Quran (binding, cover, illuminations) with gold or other decorations is permissible (la ba's). The reasoning is that it shows respect and veneration for the Quran. Sheikh Al-Quduri draws an analogy to decorating mosques with gold, which is also permissible. However, the commentary clarifies that this should not be done with the mosque's endowment funds; rather, the trustee should use his own money. If done with mosque funds, the trustee becomes liable. The earlier reference (in Hidayah) is noted.

Key Terms
تحلية (tahliya): Adorning or embellishing the Quran with gold or other decorations.
نقش (naqsh): Engraving or decorating the mosque with designs.
ماء الذهب (ma' al-dhahab): Gold water or gold leaf used for decoration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on adorning the Quran with gold according to the text?
A) Makruh (disliked).
B) Haram (forbidden).
C) La ba's (no harm).
D) Sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Takeaway
Adorning the Quran with gold is permissible in the Hanafi school because it expresses veneration and is analogised to decorating mosques.

Entry of Dhimmis into Mosques: Hanafi vs Shafi'i vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on mosque entry for non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmis entering mosques, explain the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and evaluate the Hanafi critique of their proofs.

Core Idea
Dhimmis may enter any mosque freely; the Hanafi school distinguishes them from polytheists.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on the entry of non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) into mosques, particularly Masjid al-Haram. The Hanafi school holds a permissive position, while al-Shafi'i and Malik restrict access. Understanding their proofs reveals how each school weighs scriptural texts and legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling: 'la ba's' (no harm) for dhimmis to enter Masjid al-Haram and any other mosque.
2
Identify the opposing positions
Al-Shafi'i says makruh for Masjid al-Haram but allows other mosques; Malik says makruh in every mosque.
3
Examine al-Shafi'i's proof
Quran 9:28 ('polytheists are impure') and the janabah argument (the disbeliever never purifies).
The verse restricts Masjid al-Haram; janabah is an additional reasoning.
4
Analyze Malik's extension
Malik generalizes the impurity (najis) to all mosques, taking the 'illah as general.
This leads to a broader prohibition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi critique points out inconsistency: if janabah is the reason, why allow other mosques? The verse is specific to polytheists and to Masjid al-Haram, not dhimmis.
The Hanafi school maintains original permissibility (ibahah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا بأس بان يدخل اهل الذمة المسجد الحرام وقال الشافعي يكره ذلك وقال مالک یکرہ فی کل مسجد للشافعي قوله تعالى انما المشركون نجس فلا يقربوا المسجد الحرام بعد عامهم هذا ولان الكافر لا يخلو عن جنابة لانه لا يغتسل اغتسالا يخرجه عنها والجنب يجنب المسجد وبهذا يحتج مالك والتعليل بالنجاسة عام فينتظم المساجد كلها
He said: There is no harm for dhimmis to enter Masjid al-Haram. And al-Shafi'i said: That is disliked. And Malik said: It is disliked in every mosque. For al-Shafi'i is the saying of Allah: 'Indeed the polytheists are impure, so let them not approach Masjid al-Haram after this year of theirs.' And because the disbeliever is never free from janabah, for he does not perform a ghusl that would remove him from it, and the junub is kept away from the mosque. And with this Malik argues. And the explanation by impurity is general, so it encompasses all mosques.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents a three-school dispute regarding the entry of non-Muslims (dhimmis) into mosques. The Hanafi school, represented by Imam Muhammad, rules that there is no harm in dhimmis entering even Masjid al-Haram (the Sacred Mosque in Mecca). Imam al-Shafi'i considers it disliked (makruh) for Masjid al-Haram but allows entry into other mosques. Imam Malik considers it disliked in all mosques. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the Quranic verse (9:28) stating polytheists are impure and should not approach Masjid al-Haram, and the argument that disbelievers are perpetually in a state of janabah (major impurity) because they do not perform proper ghusl, and a junub person is prevented from the mosque. Malik extends this reasoning by taking the 'illah (cause) of impurity as general, applying to all mosques. However, the Hanafi response (implied in the commentary) criticizes al-Shafi'i's position as inconsistent: if janabah is the reason, why allow entry into other mosques? The Hanafi school does not accept this reasoning and maintains permissibility, either because the impurity is not physical or because the prohibition on the Quran verse is specific to polytheists and applies only to Masjid al-Haram at that time. The position is that dhimmis are not 'nabis' in the same sense, and their entry is allowed based on the principle of original permissibility.

Key Terms
أهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimma): Protected non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state.
المشركون (al-mushrikun): Polytheists; those who associate partners with Allah.
نجس (najis): Ritually impure.
جنابة (janaba): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
مسجد الحرام (Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque in Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, what is the ruling on dhimmis entering Masjid al-Haram?
A) Haram (forbidden).
B) Makruh (disliked).
C) La ba's (no harm).
D) Only during certain times.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits dhimmis to enter all mosques, distinguishing them from polytheists who are only prohibited from Masjid al-Haram.

Ruling on Employing Eunuchs
States ruling and reason for karahah of employing eunuchs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on employing eunuchs and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind it using the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).

Core Idea
Employing eunuchs is makruh because it encourages muthlah (castration), which is haram.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Quduri on the permissibility of employing eunuchs. While the employment itself may seem neutral, the Hanafi school considers the broader consequences. The underlying reason (talil) is the fear of promoting the prohibited act of muthlah. Understanding this helps us see how fiqh uses the principle of blocking the means (sadd al-dhara'i').

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the source passage to determine which act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification (hukm) is.
The act is 'employing eunuchs' (istikhdam al-khisyān). The ruling is makruh (disliked).
2
Identify the reason (talil)
Locate the phrase 'li-anna al-raghbata ...' which provides the legal cause for the ruling.
The reason is that it creates a desire in people to practice castration (muthlah).
3
Understand the basis of the prohibition of muthlah
The text states that muthlah is haram (prohibited). Recognize that castration is a form of mutilation explicitly forbidden in Islamic sources.
Muthlah includes any disfigurement; its prohibition is established by Quran and Hadith.
4
Apply the principle of sadd al-dhara'i'
Connect the ruling to the usul principle that blocking means to evil is a valid basis for restriction.
Even though employment itself is permissible, it becomes makruh because it leads to haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خصی سے خدمت لینے کا حکم
قال و يكره استخدام الخصيان لان الرغبة فى استخدام حت الناس على هذا الصنيع وهو مثله محرمة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اور خصیوں سے خدمت لینا مکروہ ہے اس لئے کہ ان سے خدمت لینے میں رغبت کرنا لوگوں کو ابھی حرکیت ، پر ابھارنا ہے حالانکہ یہ مثلہ ہونا ہے جو حرام ہے۔ تشریح یعنی جولوگ خصیے نکلوا کر ہیجڑے اور خصی ہو جاتے ہیں ان سے خدمت لینا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ جب ان سے خدمت کی جائے گی تو دوسرے لوگوں کو رغبت ہوگی کہ یہ تو آمدنی کا ذریعہ ہے تو وہ بھی ہیجڑے بنیں گے۔ حالانکہ یہ حرام ہے کیونکہ یہ مثلہ ہونا ہے جس کی ممانعت مصرح ہے۔
Ruling on employing eunuchs: He (al-Quduri) said: It is disliked to employ eunuchs, because desiring employment (of them) leads people to this practice, and it is muthlah (mutilation) which is prohibited. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Employing eunuchs is makruh because desiring service from them encourages people to this act, while it is muthlah which is haram. Explanation: Employing those who have been castrated is makruh because when they are employed, others will be motivated to become eunuchs as a source of income, while this act is haram due to being muthlah which is explicitly prohibited.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on employing eunuchs (castrated males). Al-Quduri rules it is makruh (disliked). The reason is that employing them creates demand, encouraging others to undergo castration (muthlah), which is haram. The commentary emphasizes the prohibition of muthlah, which refers to disfiguring or mutilating the body. The karahah here is likely tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) because the act of employment itself is not inherently haram, but it leads to haram. The Hanafi position is that one should avoid employing eunuchs to prevent the spread of this forbidden practice.

Key Terms
مثلہ (muthlah): Mutilation or disfigurement of the body; here specifically castration.
کراہت (karāhah): Legal dislike; here makruh tanzihi meaning discouraged but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is employing eunuchs makruh according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are impure.
B) Because it encourages the haram act of muthlah (castration).
C) Because they are not trustworthy.
D) Because it is similar to employing prostitutes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on employing eunuchs illustrates how the principle of blocking means (sadd al-dhara'i') turns a neutral act into a disliked one due to its harmful consequences.

Ruling on Castrating Animals and Mating Donkeys with Horses
Ruling permissibility with proof from prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on castrating animals and hybrid mating, and explain the proof from the Prophet's riding a mule.

Core Idea
The Prophet's riding a mule proves the permissibility of producing it.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a clear ruling: both castration of animals and mating donkeys with horses to produce mules are permissible. The reasoning is based on benefit for the first and prophetic example for the second. This lesson unpacks the proof (dalil) and the legal reasoning (istidlal) that connects the Prophet's action to the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions and their ruling
The text states that there is no harm (la ba's) in castrating animals and mating donkeys with mares. This indicates legal permissibility (ibahah).
The term 'la ba's' in Hanafi fiqh often means mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the Prophet's (peace be upon him) riding a mule. The mule is the product of hybrid mating between a donkey and a horse.
This hadith is narrated in multiple authentic collections, e.g., Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how it proves)
The argument is: If the act of hybrid mating were haram, the Prophet would not have ridden the mule, because that would indirectly endorse or open the door to a prohibited act. Since he did ride it, the act of producing the mule must be permissible.
This is an inference from prophetic action (fi'l) indicating permissibility.
4
Understand the benefit reasoning for castration
Castration is permitted because it benefits the animal (fattening) and people (safety from aggression). The Hanafi school considers benefit (manfa'ah) as a basis for permissibility.
This distinguishes castration from prohibited mutilation (muthlah).
5
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to any similar beneficial action, not just the specific cases mentioned. The principle is: if the means to a permissible end is beneficial, it is allowed.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس باخصاء البهائم و انزاء الحمير على الخيل لان في الأول منفعة البهيمة والناس وقد صح ان النبي عليه السلام ركب البغلة فلو كان هذا الفعل حراماً لما ركبها لما فيه من فتح بابه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور چوپایوں کو خصی کرنے میں اور گدھوں کو گھوڑی پر چڑھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ اول میں چوپائے اور لوگوں کی منفعت ہے اور یہ بات صحیح ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام خچر پر سوار ہوئے۔ پس اگر یہ فعل حرام ہوتا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم خچر پر سوار نہ ہوتے وجہ اس کے کہ اس میں اس کے دروازہ کو کھولنا ہے۔ تشریح جانور کو خصی کرنے میں جانور کا بھی فائدہ ہے کہ وہ خوب موٹا تازہ ہوتا ہے اور انسانوں کا بھی فائدہ ہے کہ اس کے شر سے محفوظ رہتے ہیں نیز گدھے کو گھوڑی پر چڑھانا تا کہ خچر پیدا آجائے جائز ہے کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم خچر پر سوار ہوئے ہیں اگر یہ کام حرام ہوتا تو آپ خچر پر سوار نہ ہوتے کہ اس فعل ممنوع کا دروازہ نہ کھل جائے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: There is no harm in castrating animals and mounting donkeys on mares, because in the first there is benefit for the animal and people, and it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) rode a mule. If this act were prohibited, he would not have ridden it, because of opening its door. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Castrating animals and mating donkeys with mares is not objectionable, because in the former there is benefit for the animal and people, and it is authentic that the Prophet (peace be upon him) rode a mule. If this act were prohibited, he would not have ridden it, for it would open the door to that act. Explanation: Castration benefits the animal by fattening and people by safety; mating donkey and horse to produce a mule is permissible because the Prophet rode a mule.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage rules on two actions: castration of animals and hybrid mating (donkey with horse to produce mules). Al-Quduri states there is no harm (la ba's) in either. The reason for castration is benefit: the animal becomes fatter, and people are protected from its aggression. For hybridization, the proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) rode a mule, which is a product of such mating. The argument is that if the act of mating a donkey with a horse were haram, the Prophet would not have ridden the mule, as that would indirectly endorse the act. Thus, both actions are permissible. The Hanafi school considers these as mubah (permissible) due to benefit and prophetic practice.

Key Terms
إخصاء البهائم (ikhsa' al-baha'im): Castration of animals for benefit.
إنزاء الحمير على الخيل (inza' al-humir 'ala al-khayl): Mating donkeys with mares to produce mules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof for the permissibility of mating donkeys with horses?
A) The Prophet commanded it.
B) The Prophet rode a mule, which is the product of such mating.
C) It is mentioned in the Quran.
D) There is no proof; it is only istihsan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits castration and hybrid mating based on benefit and prophetic example, using the principle that what is permissible by prophetic action is itself permissible.

Ruling on Visiting Sick Jews and Christians
Ruling with proof from prophetic action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on visiting sick non-Muslims and identify the prophetic evidence for it.

Core Idea
Visiting a sick Jew or Christian is permissible as an act of kindness, proven by the Prophet's own example.

What should a Muslim do when a non-Muslim neighbor or colleague falls ill? Some may hesitate, thinking visiting them is prohibited or shows partiality. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, grounded in the Qur'anic principle of birr (kindness) and the prophetic practice of visiting a sick Jewish neighbor. We will see that such visits are not only allowed but can be an act of righteousness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the explicit ruling: 'There is no harm' (la ba's) in visiting a Jew or Christian. This indicates permissibility (ibaha).
The Arabic phrase 'la ba's' is commonly used in Hanafi fiqh for mubah (permissible) acts.
2
Understand the Rationale
The text explains the reason: it is a type of birr (kindness/righteousness). Birr is encouraged towards all people, including non-Muslims, as long as it does not compromise Islamic principles.
Birr is a broad concept; the Qur'an uses it for acts of goodness.
3
Locate the Proof
The proof is a prophetic hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) visited a sick Jewish neighbor. This is a direct demonstration (fi'l) of permissibility.
The hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections.
4
Note the Scope and Exceptions
The commentary extends the ruling to all disbelievers except Magians, where there is a difference of narration (the correct view is permissibility). Also, visiting a sinful Muslim is permissible, but if the patient finds visits burdensome, it becomes makruh.
The Makruh ruling is based on the principle of avoiding harm (darar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا بأس بعيادة اليهودي والنصراني لانه نوع برفى حقهم ومانهينا عن ذلك وصح ان النبي عليه السلام عاديهوديا مرض بجواره
ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر فرمایا ہے اور یہودی اور نصرانی کی عیادت کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ بھلائی کی ایک قسم ہے اور ہم اس سے منع نہیں کیے گئے ہیں اور یہ بات صحیح ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے ایک یہودی کی عیادت فرمائی تھی جو آپ کے پڑوس میں بیمار ہو گیا تھا۔ تشریح یہودی و نصرانی یا کوئی اور کافر کی عیادت کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ اسلام بھلائی کا کام کرنے سے نہیں روکتا اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہودی کی عیادت کرنا ثابت ہے اگر چہ مجوس کی عیادت میں احناف کے دو قول ہیں مگر جو از اصح ہے اور اسی طرح فاسق کی عیادت جائز ہے اسلئے کہ وہ مسلمان ہے اور عیادت حقوق مسلمین میں سے ہے البتہ اگر مریض کو آنے والوں سے گرانی ہوتی ہو تو ایسی صورت میں عیادت مکروہ ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۴۸ ج ۵
He (al-Quduri) said: There is no harm in visiting a Jew or Christian, because it is a type of kindness (birr) towards them, and we have not been prohibited from that, and it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) visited a sick Jew who was his neighbor. Translation: Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: There is no harm in visiting a Jew or Christian... Explanation: There is no harm in visiting Jews, Christians, or other disbelievers in the sense of kindness...
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage rules on visiting a sick Jew or Christian. It is permissible (la ba's) as an act of kindness (birr). The proof is the hadith that the Prophet himself visited a sick Jewish neighbor. The commentary adds that this applies to all disbelievers except Magians, concerning whom there are two narrations in the Hanafi school (the correct one is permissibility). Visiting a sinful Muslim is also permissible as it is a right of Muslims, but if the patient finds visits burdensome, it becomes makruh. This ruling is based on the general principle of ihsan (good treatment) and the specific prophetic example.

Key Terms
بر (birr): Kindness, righteousness; acts of good treatment towards others, including non-Muslims.
عيادة (iyadah): Visiting the sick; a recommended act in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Core Idea
Using unsubstantiated expressions in dua is makruh; the phrase 'knot of honor' is disliked for its anthropomorphic implication.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar regarding supplication wording. The author states that saying 'I ask You by the knot of honor from Your Throne' is makruh. We will explore why this phrase is considered objectionable and how the Hanafi school approaches dua etiquette. The passage is incomplete, but the ruling is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the verbal statement during supplication. The ruling is explicitly stated as 'makruh' (disliked).

2

The text mentions two versions of the phrase: 'بمعقد العز' (knot of honor) and 'مقعد العز' (seat of honor). Both carry the same ruling.
These variations do not change the ruling.
3

While the reason is not fully stated in the excerpt, Hanafi commentators explain that such phrases may imply a physical location or attribute for Allah (tashbih) and are not authentically reported from the Prophet ﷺ.
The principle: avoid expressions that are not grounded in the Quran or Sunna and that may lead to improper beliefs.
4
Relate to general dua etiquette
The Hanafi school emphasizes using authentic supplications and avoiding innovated phrases. This ruling is part of that broader discipline.
Adhere to the Sunna in wording and meaning.

Ruling on Employing Castrated Servants
Ruling statement with causal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on employing castrated men and explain the reasoning based on sadd al-dhara'i'.

Core Idea
Employing a castrated man is makruh because it encourages mutilation, which is haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on employing castrated men (khusy). Imam al-Quduri's matn declares it makruh (disliked). The commentary explains that the underlying reason is to block the means (sadd al-dhara'i') to the prohibited act of mutilation (muthla). Understanding this ruling helps us see how Islamic law prevents harm even in indirect ways.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State that the act of employing a castrated man (khusy) is ruled makruh tanzih (disliked) in the Hanafi school. Note that the ruling is from Al-Quduri's matn, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Analyze the ta'lil (reasoning)
The text provides the cause: employing such individuals creates a demand and encourages others to undergo castration. Castration is a form of muthla (mutilation), which is explicitly haram.
The reasoning is based on sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil).
3
Apply the ruling in context
Consider modern parallels: employing a eunuch for non-medical reasons carries the same disliked ruling. If there is a genuine need (e.g., medical custody), the ruling may differ, but the source does not discuss exceptions.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is makruh, as per the Hanafi school.

Source Text

Book of Disliked Acts. Page 390. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 13. Ruling on employing castrated servants. He said: It is disliked to employ castrated men because desire in employing them incites people to this act, and it is like mutilation which is forbidden. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is disliked to employ castrated men because desiring to employ them incites people to this action, whereas this is mutilation (muthla) which is haram. Explanation: That is, it is disliked to employ those who have had their testicles removed and become eunuchs or castrated, because when they are employed, others will desire thinking it is a source of income, so they too will become eunuchs. However, this is haram because it is a form of mutilation which is explicitly prohibited.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the employment of castrated men (khusyan). The passage type is a ruling statement with reasoning. Imam al-Quduri's matn states that it is makruh (disliked) to employ such individuals. The commentary explains that the underlying reason is that employing them creates a demand for castration, which in turn encourages others to undergo this procedure. Since castration (specifically the removal of testicles) is considered a form of mutilation (muthla), which is explicitly prohibited in Islamic law, any action that leads to its proliferation is also disliked. The ruling is based on the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil). The Hanafi position is clear: the act itself is not haram, but it is makruh tanzihan due to its consequences.

Key Terms
خصي (khusy): A castrated male, specifically one whose testicles have been removed.
استخدام (istikhdam): Employing or using someone for service.
مثلہ (muthla): Mutilation, specifically the cutting off of body parts without medical necessity.

Castrating Animals and Crossbreeding Donkeys with Horses: A Hanafi Ruling with Proof
Ruling on castrating animals and crossbreeding donkeys and horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on castrating animals and crossbreeding donkeys with horses, and explain the proof from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
Castrating animals and breeding mules are permissible due to benefit and prophetic precedent.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school on two practical matters: castration of animals and crossbreeding to produce mules. The matn of al-Quduri declares them permissible, and the commentary supports it with a powerful proof from the Prophetic sunnah. You will see how the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) is used as a legal indicator of permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
The matn explicitly states that both castrating animals (ikhsa' al-baha'im) and mating donkeys with horses (inza' al-humayr 'ala al-khayl) are permissible (la ba's). Note that this is the direct ruling from the text.
The ruling is mubah – permissible, not obligatory or recommended.
2
Understand the first proof: benefit
The text gives two reasons for permissibility. First, there is benefit (manfa'ah) for the animal (it becomes fatter and more useful) and for people (they are protected from its aggression and gain a useful beast of burden). In Hanafi usul, benefit (maslahah) is a valid basis for permissibility unless prohibited.
Benefit must be genuine and not outweighed by harm.
3
Understand the second proof: prophetic action
The text cites that the Prophet Muhammad rode a mule (baghlah). Since a mule is the offspring of a donkey and a horse, the Prophet's action indicates that the act of producing it is permissible. If it were forbidden, he would not have ridden it, as that would imply tacit approval of a forbidden act.
This is an example of taqrir – the Prophet's silent approval of something.
4
Apply the principle of taqrir
The reasoning is: the Prophet's riding the mule is a tacit approval of the means that produced it. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions (af'al) and tacit approvals (taqrir) are sources of law indicating permissibility (ibahah). This proof is strong (qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah).
Taqrir is a type of Sunnah that shows the act is not forbidden.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
While the Hanafi school permits both actions, some other schools may consider castration makruh without necessity. The difference stems from weighing benefit versus potential harm (pain to the animal). The Hanafi position prioritizes the clear benefit and prophetic precedent.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس باخصاء البهائم و انزاء الحمير على الخيل لان في الأول منفعة البهيمة والناس وقد صح ان النبي عليه السلام ركب البغلة فلو كان هذا الفعل حراماً لما ركبها لما فيه من فتح بابه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور چوپایوں کو خصی کرنے میں اور گدھوں کو گھوڑی پر چڑھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ اول میں چوپائے اور لوگوں کی منفعت ہے اور یہ بات صحیح ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام خچر پر سوار ہوئے۔ پس اگر یہ فعل حرام ہوتا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم خچر پر سوار نہ ہوتے ہوجہ اس کے کہ اس میں اس کے دروازہ کو کھولنا ہے۔
He said: There is no harm in castrating animals and in mating donkeys with horses, because in the first there is benefit for the animal and people, and it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) rode a mule. If this act were forbidden, he would not have ridden it, because that would open the door to the forbidden act.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses two actions: castrating animals and crossbreeding donkeys with horses to produce mules. The matn by al-Quduri declares both actions permissible (la ba's). The commentary provides two proofs: first, there is a benefit – for the animal (it becomes fatter) and for people (they are protected from its aggressiveness, and the mule is a useful animal). Second, the Prophet Muhammad himself rode a mule, which is the offspring of a donkey and a horse. If the act of crossbreeding were forbidden, the Prophet would not have ridden the mule, as that would imply tacit approval of a forbidden act. This reasoning is based on the principle that the Prophet's actions (taqrir) indicate permissibility. The ruling is clear: both actions are mubah (permissible).

Key Terms
اخصاء البهائم (ikhsa' al-baha'im): Castration of animals, removing their testicles or ovaries.
انزاء الحمير على الخيل (inza' al-humayr 'ala al-khayl): Mating donkeys with horses to produce mules.
بغلة (baghla): A mule, the offspring of a male donkey and a female horse.

The Hanafi Ruling on Supplicating with 'بمعقد العز من عرشك'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on supplication phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the supplication phrase 'بمعقد العز من عرشك' and explain why it is considered makruh despite a narrated hadith from the Prophet.

Core Idea
Supplicating with 'بمعقد العز من عرشك' is makruh because it implies attaching Allah's honor to a created entity (the Throne).

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of using specific phrases in supplication. Imam Muhammad's matn in al-Jami' al-Saghir rules the phrase 'اسألك بمعقد العز من عرشك' as makruh. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, permits it due to a narrated hadith. By analyzing the linguistic implications and the reliability of the hadith, we will understand why the Hanafi school prefers the ruling of makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling in the Matn
Read Imam Muhammad's clear statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'ويكره ان يقول الرجل في دعائه اسألك بمعقد العزمن عرشك' – it is disliked. This is the starting point.
Makruh here means makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) due to the problematic implication.
2
Understand the Linguistic Problem
Analyze the two expressions: 'معقد العز' (knot of honor) and 'مقعد العز' (seat of honor). The second clearly implies sitting (qu'ud) and is definitely anthropomorphic. The first implies that honor is tied to the Throne, which is created, thus implying that Allah's attribute of honor is temporal (hadith).
Since the Throne is created, attaching honor to it suggests that honor itself is created, which is invalid.
3
Note the Opposing View of Imam Abu Yusuf
Imam Abu Yusuf (and later Faqih Abu al-Layth) considered the phrase permissible because it is narrated from the Prophet's supplication: 'اللهم إني أسألك بمعقد العز من عرشك...'.
This shows that within the Hanafi school, there is a difference of opinion based on evidence (dalil).
4
Analyze the Proof: Khabar Wahid vs. Fabrication
The commentator responds that the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and was judged fabricated (mawdu') by Ibn al-Jawzi. Even if authentic, precaution (ihtiyat) requires abstaining because the phrase leads to a dangerous meaning.
In Hanafi usul, khabar wahid is accepted for practice only if not contradicted by stronger evidence or linguistic problems.
5
Apply the Principle of Precaution
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Imam Muhammad: it is makruh. The harm from a possible false attribute outweighs the benefit of using a weak hadith. Additionally, any supplication using 'بحق فلان' (by the right of someone) is also makruh for similar reasons.
The general rule: avoid any phrase that might imply deficiency or anthropomorphism in Allah.

امام ابو یوسف کا نقطہ نظر

امام ابو یوسف کے استدلال کا جواب
ولكنا نقول هذا خبر الواحد وكان الاحتياط في الامتناع ويكره ان يقول في دعائه بحق فلان او بحق انبیائک ورسلك لانه لا حق للمخلوق على الخالق.
ترجمہ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ خبر واحد ہے تو احتیاط رکنے میں ہے اور مکروہ ہے کہ اپنی دعا میں کہے بحق فلان یا بحق انبیائک ورسلك
Ruling on saying in supplication 'I ask You by the knot of honor from Your Throne'. He (Imam Muhammad) said: It is disliked for a man to say in his supplication 'I ask You by the knot of honor from Your Throne'. The question has two expressions: this one and 'maq'ad al-'izz'. There is no doubt about the dislike of the second because it is derived from qu'ud (sitting). Similarly, the first is disliked because it gives the impression that His honor is attached to the Throne, while the Throne is created and Allah with all His attributes is eternal. Explanation: Saying words in supplication that imply shirk or deficiency in the divine essence is makruh. Allah with all His attributes is eternal, and the entire universe is created, including the Throne and Kursi. So using such words that imply that honor is specific to the Throne or that the Throne is a place of honor is makruh due to ambiguity. Thus, both phrases are makruh. The first because 'mu'qad' implies a place of tying, suggesting the Throne is a locus for tying honor, implying temporality. The second because it implies sitting on the Throne, which is the view of anthropomorphists. We have discussed this in detail in Jawahir al-Fara'id. Imam Abu Yusuf's viewpoint: From Abu Yusuf, there is no harm in it, and Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted this because it is transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him). It is narrated that among his supplications was: 'O Allah, I ask You by the knot of honor from Your Throne, the utmost mercy from Your Book, by Your Greatest Name, Your Supreme Majesty, and Your Perfect Words.' Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf considered it permissible and proved these words from transmitted supplications. I say: Al-Bayhaqi narrated it in al-Da'awat al-Kabir, and Ibn al-Jawzi included it in al-Mawdu'at. Ibn al-Jawzi said: This hadith is fabricated without doubt, and its chain is confused. See Nasb al-Rayah vol. 4 p. 273. Response to Imam Abu Yusuf's argument: But we say: This is a solitary report (khabar wahid), and precaution is to abstain. And it is disliked to say in his supplication 'by the right of so-and-so' or 'by the right of Your prophets and messengers', because there is no right of the created upon the Creator.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding specific supplication phrases. The matn by Imam Muhammad in Al-Jami' al-Saghir rules that it is makruh to say 'اسألك بمعقد العز من عرشك' (I ask You by the knot of honor from Your Throne) and its variant 'مقعد العز'. The reasoning is that such phrases imply that Allah's attribute of honor is attached to the Throne (which is created) or that Allah sits on the Throne (tajsim). Since Allah is eternal and free from spatial location, these phrases are avoided. Then the commentary presents the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who considers it permissible because it is narrated from the Prophet. However, the disputing scholars (the commentator) argue that this hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and is considered fabricated (mawdu') by scholars like Ibn al-Jawzi. Therefore, precaution dictates abstaining. Moreover, the commentary extends the ruling to any supplication using 'بحق' (by the right of) someone, because no creature has a right upon the Creator. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one stated in the matn: it is makruh.

Key Terms
معقد العز (mu'qad al-'izz): The knot or tie of honor, implying the Throne as the location where honor is tied or attached.
مقعد العز (maq'ad al-'izz): The seat of honor, implying sitting or resting on the Throne.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith, i.e., a report not reaching the level of tawatur.
بحق فلان (bi haqqi fulan): By the right of so-and-so, invoking a person's claim on Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the supplication phrase 'اسألك بمعقد العز من عرشك'?
A) It is permissible (mubah) because it is from the Prophet.
B) It is disliked (makruh) because it implies anthropomorphism.
C) It is forbidden (haram) because it is shirk.
D) It is recommended (sunnah) because the Prophet said it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits supplication phrases that imply temporality or anthropomorphism, even if reported in a weak hadith; precaution in creed takes precedence.

Ruling on Supplicating with 'Bi-Ma'qid al-'Izz' and Similar Phrases
Intra-Hanafi dispute on karahah of supplicatory phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplicatory phrases implying temporal or spatial attributes of Allah and explain why Abu Yusuf's permissive view is not adopted.

Core Idea
Phrases suggesting temporal or spatial attributes of Allah are disliked, even if reported in weak hadith.

This lesson addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding certain supplicatory phrases. While some may consider these phrases harmless, the Hanafi school emphasizes precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid any implication of deficiency in Allah's attributes. We will examine the reasoning behind the majority view and its response to a dissenting opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two supplicatory phrases
Recognize 'ma'qid al-'izz' (the place where honor is tied) and 'maq'ad al-'izz' (the sitting place of honor). Note that the latter is explicitly anthropomorphic and unequivocally disliked.
Both phrases are derived from Arabic roots implying attachment or sitting.
2
State the majority Hanafi ruling and its basis
Imam Muhammad ruled both as makruh because they suggest that Allah's attribute of honor is tied to the created Throne, implying temporality (hadath) — which contradicts the eternity of Allah and His attributes.
This is based on the principle of avoiding tawhim (suggesting imperfection).
3
Present Abu Yusuf's dissenting view
Imam Abu Yusuf considered such phrases permissible, citing a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) used similar wording: 'O Allah, I ask You by the place of honor tied to Your Throne...'
This view was adopted by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The majority response: the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) with a weak chain (declared mawdu' by Ibn al-Jawzi). It cannot override the established principle of avoiding tawhim. Precaution (ihtiyat) requires refraining.
The weaker chain does not meet the standard for permissibility in matters of 'aqidah.
5
Extend the ruling to similar phrases
The same precaution applies to saying 'bi-haqqi fulan' (by the right of so-and-so) in supplication, as no created being has a right over the Creator. However, if intended as tawassul (seeking means), some scholars interpret it as permissible, but the majority prohibit absolutely.
This extension shows the school's consistency in blocking means to potential shirk.

The second [phrase] is disliked because it is derived from al-qu'ud (sitting), and similarly the first [phrase] is disliked because it suggests the attachment of His honor to the Throne, while the Throne is created and Allah, with all His attributes, is eternal. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is disliked that a person says in his supplication: 'I ask You by Your honor tied to Your Throne.' There are two expressions: one is this, and the second is 'maq'ad al-'izz' (the sitting place of honor). There is no doubt about the second being disliked because it is derived from qu'ud. Similarly, the first is disliked because it suggests that divine honor is attached to the Throne, whereas the Throne is created and Allah, with all His attributes, is eternal. Explanation: It is disliked to say words in supplication that suggest shirk or imply a deficiency in the majesty of Allah. Allah, with all His attributes, is eternal, and the entire universe is created, including the Throne and the Kursi. So using words that make honor appear tied to them or that make a place of honor known is disliked due to ambiguity. Therefore, supplicating with 'as'aluka bi-ma'qid al-'izz min 'arshika' or 'as'aluka bi-maq'ad al-'izz min 'arshika' is disliked. The first is because 'ma'qid' is derived from 'aqd' (tie), meaning the place of tying, so it means the place where honor is tied to the Throne. Calling the Throne the place of tying honor suggests that it is created, because the Throne is not eternal but created; then honor attached to the Throne would also be created, but it is invalid for it to be a locus of temporal events. The second case: 'maq'ad' is derived from 'qu'ud' (sitting), meaning the sitting place on the Throne, i.e., the Throne is the place of honor. In this case, the Throne would be established as a place for the possible [i.e., a body], which is the statement of the anthropomorphists and is utterly false. And from Abu Yusuf: There is no harm in it, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted it because it is reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him. It is narrated that among his supplications was: 'O Allah, I ask You by the place of honor tied to Your Throne, and the utmost mercy from Your Book, and by Your Greatest Name, Your Supreme Majesty, and Your Complete Words.' Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that there is no harm in it, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted it because it is transmitted from the Prophet, peace be upon him. It is narrated that part of his supplication was: 'O Allah, I ask You by the place of honor tied to Your Throne, the utmost mercy from Your Book, by Your Greatest Name, Your Supreme Glory, and Your Complete Words.' Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf considered it permissible and established these words as a transmitted supplication. I say: Al-Bayhaqi narrated it in al-Da'awat al-Kabir, and Ibn al-Jawzi narrated it in al-Mawdu'at. Ibn al-Jawzi said: This hadith is unquestionably fabricated, and its chain is confused, as you see in Nasb al-Rayah vol. 4 p. 273. But we say: This is khabar wahid, and precaution is in refraining, and it is disliked to say in his supplication 'By the right of so-and-so' or 'by the right of Your prophets and messengers' because the created has no right over the Creator. Translation: But we say this is a solitary report, so precaution is in abstaining, and it is disliked to say in one's supplication 'by the right of so-and-so' or 'by the right of Your prophets and messengers' because the created has no right over the Creator. Explanation: This is a response to Imam Abu Yusuf, and the earlier response is better, which concludes that the hadith is not a proof. Then, the custom of saying in supplication 'by the right of so-and-so' is disliked because no one has any right over Allah; rather, whatever He gives is pure grace. So reflect. Warning: In al-Askab al-Anhar vol. 2 p. 485, it is said that its occurrence is frequent. So let it be remembered. But if 'haqq' is not taken in the sense that the mind understands, but rather honor and greatness are intended by other words as a means (wasilah), then there is no harm, and in the chains of our mashayikh where this usage occurs, it is only in the sense of tawassul, and wasilah is permissible. Allamah Shami referred to this interpretation in Radd al-Muhtar vol. 5 p. 254, then said: All such possibilities are contrary to the immediate understanding, therefore our imams have absolutely prohibited it. I say: But using it in our language in the sense of tawassul is clear, so the ruling of karahah will not apply, especially since it is supported by a hadith: 'O Allah, I ask You by the right of those who ask upon You and by the right of my walking to You.' The hadith is in Radd al-Muhtar vol. 5 p. 254.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of certain supplicatory phrases. It begins by stating the ruling of Imam Muhammad (representing the majority of the school) that it is makruh (disliked) to say 'I ask You by the honor tied to Your Throne' or 'I ask You by the sitting place of honor from Your Throne.' The reason for the first is that it suggests that Allah's attribute of 'Izz (Honor) is tied to the Throne, which is created, implying that the attribute is temporal (hadith). The second phrase is even worse because it implies that Allah sits on the Throne, which is anthropomorphism (tashbih). Both are therefore makruh due to their suggestive nature (tawhim). Then it reports the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who considered it permissible because the Prophet himself is reported to have used such phrases in his supplication. The passage then presents the Hanafi refutation: the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and has been declared fabricated by Ibn al-Jawzi; hence it cannot override the principle of avoiding anything that suggests imperfection of Allah. Precaution (ihtiyat) requires abstaining. The passage also extends the ruling to saying 'by the right of so-and-so' in supplication, which is makruh because no created being has a right upon the Creator. However, if the word 'haqq' is meant as 'honor' or 'sanctity' as a means of tawassul, some scholars allow it, but the majority of Hanafi imams prohibit it absolutely. The final note clarifies that using such phrases in the sense of tawassul in Urdu may be exempt from karahah if supported by a hadith, but caution is advised.

Key Terms
معقد العز (ma'qid al-'izz): 'The place where honor is tied/gathered' — a phrase used in supplication implying that Allah's honor is attached to the Throne.
مقعد العز (maq'ad al-'izz): 'The sitting place of honor' — implies that Allah sits on the Throne, which is anthropomorphism.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling on supplicating with 'bi-ma'qid al-'izz min 'arshika'?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that any supplicatory phrase suggesting a temporal or spatial attribute of Allah is disliked, even if it appears in a weak hadith.

Hanafi Ruling on Chess and Backgammon: An Inter-Madhhab Analysis
Hanafi ruling on games with inter-madhhab dispute on chess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on playing chess and backgammon, explain the two proofs for karahah, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Playing chess is makruh in the Hanafi school; idle amusement is forbidden unless it is for training, archery, or marital play.

The passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common question: what is the Islamic ruling on playing games like chess and backgammon? Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani states clearly that all such pastimes are disliked (makruh) because they are either gambling or idle amusement. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof and contrasts it with a reported Shafi'i view that permits chess for its intellectual benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and Hanafi ruling
What specific games are being discussed? Chess, backgammon, and a game called 'fourteen'. The ruling is karahah (disliked) according to Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Note: karahah here is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Understand the dual reasoning
The passage gives two scenarios: (1) if gambling (maisir) is involved, it is haram by Quranic text; (2) if no gambling, it is idle amusement (abath wa lahw), which is also prohibited by hadith.
The term 'maisir' covers all forms of gambling.
3
Examine the primary proof
The hadith 'لهو المؤمن باطل إلا ثلاث' limits permissible pastime to three activities. All other games are therefore batil (invalid), which in Hanafi usul implies karahah.
Consult the Dalil Block for the full text.
4
Examine the opposing view
Some scholars, including Imam al-Shafi'i, reportedly permit chess because it sharpens the intellect (tashhidh al-khawatir). Their proof is based on benefit.
This is a ikhtilaf on the permissibility of chess.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter with a stronger textual proof (the hadith about dipping hand in pig's blood) and the principle that all idle play is prohibited. Therefore, karahah is the relied-upon view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'is may allow chess; Hanafis consider it makruh.

قال ويكره اللعب بالشطرنج والنردو الاربعة عشر وكل لهو لانه ان قامر بها فالميسر حرام بالنص وهو اسم لكل قمار وان لم يقامر بها فهو عبث ولهو وقال عليه السلام لهو المؤمن باطل الا الثلاث تاديبه لفرسه ومناضلته عن قوسه وملاعبته مع اهله ترجمه امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور شطرنج اور نرد اور چودہ گوئی کھیلنا مکروہ ہے اور ہر کھیل ( مکروہ ہے ) اسلئے کہ اگر اس نے ان سے جوا کھیلا تو جو احرام ہے نص کے ساتھ اور میسر نام ہے ہر جوئے کا اور اگر جوا نہ کھیلا تو یہ عبث اور لہو ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا مؤمن کا کھیل باطل ہے مگر تین ، اس کا اپنے گھوڑے کو ادب دینا، اور اپنی کمان سے تیر پھینکنا اور اس کی ملاعبت اپنی بیوی سے۔ تشریح شطرنج اور نرد اور چودہ گوئی اور ایسے جملہ قسم کے کھیل مکروہ ہیں کیونکہ اگر ان کھیلوں میں جوئے کا پہلو ہو تو اسکی حرمت نص سے ثابت ہے اور اگر جوتے کا پہلو نہ ہوتو یہ سارے کھیل عبث واغو کام میں جو حرام ہے اور حدیث میں مؤمن کے تمام کھیلوں کو باطل کہا ہے علاوہ تین کے۔ ا شه سواری -۲- تیراندازی اپنی بیوی سے ملاعبت بعض حضرات کا مسلک وقال بعض الناس يباح اللعب بالشطرنج لما فيه من تشحيذ الخواطر وتذكية الافهام وهو محكى عن الشافعي ترجمہ اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ شطرنج کھیلنا مباح ہے اسلئے کہ اسمیں ذہنوں کو تیز کرنا اور افہام و تیز کرتا ہے۔ اور یہی منقول ہے شافعی ہے۔ تشریح بعض حضرات نے شطرنج کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اسلئے کہ اس میں ذہن تیز اور چوکس ہوتا ہے امام شافعی سے بھی یہی منقول ہے۔ احناف کی دلیل ولنا قوله عليه السلام من لعب بالشطرنج والنرد شير فكانما غمس يده فى دم الخنزير ولا نه نوع لعب
He (Imam Muhammad) said: It is disliked to play chess, backgammon, and fourteen [a game], and every pastime, because if he gambles with them, then gambling is haram by the text, and 'maisir' is the name for every gambling. And if he does not gamble with them, then it is vain and idle amusement. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The pastime of a believer is invalid except three: training his horse, shooting his bow, and playing with his wife.' Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is disliked to play chess, backgammon, and fourteen, and every game (is disliked) because if he gambles with them, then gambling is haram by the text, and 'maisir' is the name for every gambling. And if he does not gamble, then it is vain and idle amusement. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The pastime of a believer is invalid except three: training his horse, shooting his bow, and playing with his wife.' Explanation: Chess, backgammon, fourteen, and all such types of games are disliked because if they involve gambling, their prohibition is established by the text. If they do not involve gambling, then all these games are vain and idle actions which are forbidden. And in the hadith, all pastimes of a believer are said to be invalid except three: (1) horse riding, (2) archery, (3) playing with his wife. Some people's school: And some people said that playing chess is permissible because it sharpens the thoughts and stimulates the intellect, and it is reported from al-Shafi'i. Translation: And some people said that playing chess is permissible because it sharpens the thoughts and stimulates the intellect. And this is reported from al-Shafi'i. Explanation: Some people have declared chess permissible because it sharpens the mind and makes it alert. This is also reported from Imam al-Shafi'i. The evidence of the Hanafis: And our evidence is his (the Prophet's) statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever plays chess and backgammon, it is as if he dipped his hand in the blood of a pig,' and because it is a type of play.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on games, specifically chess, backgammon, and a game called 'fourteen'. It begins by stating the ruling of Imam Muhammad that playing these games is makruh (disliked). The reason is twofold: (1) if gambling is involved, it is haram because the Quran forbids maisir (gambling); (2) if no gambling is involved, it is pure idle amusement (abath) and vain play (lahw). The Prophet is reported to have said that all pastimes of a believer are invalid (batil) except three: training a horse (preparing for jihad), archery (shooting), and playing with one's wife. This hadith establishes the default prohibition of recreational games. The passage then mentions an opposing view attributed to some people, including Imam al-Shafi'i, that chess is permissible because it sharpens the intellect. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: (1) the hadith that whoever plays chess and backgammon is as if he dipped his hand in pig's blood, which indicates severe disapproval; (2) the general principle that any form of play (lahw) is invalid for a believer except the three specified. Therefore, chess remains makruh in the Hanafi school, even without gambling, because it is a waste of time and distracts from remembrance of Allah. The dispute highlights a difference in methodology: Shafi'is consider the intellectual benefit, while Hanafis emphasize avoidance of idle play and rely on the general prohibition.

Key Terms
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess; a board game of strategy.
نرد (nard): Backgammon; a dice game often associated with gambling.
میسر (maisir): Gambling; a game of chance with stakes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, what is the ruling on playing chess without any gambling?
A) Halal (permissible)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mustahabb (recommended)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, all idle amusements are makruh unless they fall within the three exceptions; chess and backgammon are makruh tanzihi even without gambling.
