Ruling on Saying 'Bi Haqqi' in Supplication
Explains the Hanafi ruling on invoking Allah by the right of others in dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying 'bi haqqi fulan' in dua and explain the conditions under which it becomes permissible through ta'wil.

Core Idea
No creature has a right over Allah, so 'bi haqqi' is disliked unless understood as tawassul.

Have you ever heard someone say 'By the right of your Prophet' in prayer? Is this permissible? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position: the literal wording implies a claim upon Allah, which is impossible, so it is makruh. However, if the phrase is understood as tawassul—seeking Allah's favor through the honor of His creation—it becomes permissible. This lesson unpacks the proof and the key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
Recognize the act: saying 'bi haqqi fulan' (by the right of so-and-so) in supplication. According to the passage, the default ruling is makruh because no created being has a right over Allah; all blessings are pure grace.
The term 'haqq' literally means a claim or due. Apply the principle: 'La haqqa li makhluq ala al-Khaliq'.
2
Examine the Evidence (Dalil)
The author cites a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Allahumma inni as'aluka bi haqqi al-sa'ileen 'alayka...' This hadith is used by some to permit the phrasing, but Hanafi scholars note its weak evidentiary value (zanni al-dalalah) and argue it refers to the 'honor' of the askers, not a literal right.
The hadith is found in Radd al-Muhtar. Its chain is ahad, making its transmission zanni.
3
Understand the Ta'wil (Interpretive Resolution)
The passage explains that if 'haqq' is interpreted as 'wasilah' (means) or as a reference to 'honor and greatness', then the ruling changes to permissible. This is because the mind no longer understands it as a claim upon Allah. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah argues that in Urdu, the phrase is naturally understood as tawassul, so the dislike does not apply.
Allamah Shami (Radd al-Muhtar) notes that the apparent meaning contradicts this ta'wil, so the imams absolutely forbade the literal wording.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
The relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school is that saying 'bi haqqi' is makruh if taken literally. However, when the context or linguistic understanding clearly indicates tawassul, it is permissible. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah favours permissibility in the Urdu context due to common usage and the supporting hadith.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad hold karahah; the later ta'wil view is a minority but accepted in certain contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و رسلک اسلئے کہ مخلوق کا کوئی حق خالق پر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کا جواب ہے اور جواب سابق اس سے عمدہ ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث قابل استدلال نہیں ہے پھر یہ جو دستور ہے کہ دعاء میں کہتے ہیں کہ بحق فلاں فلاں یہ مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اللہ پرکسی کا کوئی حق نہیں بلکہ وہ جو کچھ دیتا ہے اس کا فضل محض ہے۔ فتدبر تنبیه - ا سکب الانہر ص ۴۸۵ ج ۲ پر کہا ہے کہ اس کا وقوع بکثرت ہے۔ فلیحفظ لیکن اگر حق کو اس معنی میں نہ لیا جائے جس کی جانب ذہن کا انتقال ہوتا ہے بلکہ اس سے حرمت و عظمت بالفاظ دیگر وسیله مراد لیا جائے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور ہمارے مشائخ کے شجروں میں جہاں یہ ستعمال ہے تو وہ صرف توسل کے معنی میں ہے اور وسیلہ جائز ہے۔ علامہ شامی نے ردالمختارص ۲۵۴ ج ۵ پر اس تاویل کی جانب اشارات کر کے پھر فرمایا ہے کہ سب ایسے احتمالات ہیں جو ظاہر میں تبادر کے خلاف ہیں اسی وجہ سے ہمارے ائمہ نے مطلقا منع فرمایا ہے۔ قلت لیکن اس کو ہماری زبان میں توسل کے معنی میں استعمال کرنا ظاہر ہے تو اس پر کراہت کا حکم جاری نہ ہوگا جبکہ اس کی ایک حدیث سے بھی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے :- اللهم انی اسئلک بحق السائلین علیک و بحق ممشای الیک الحدیث في رد المحتار ص ۲۵۴ج ۵
And your messenger because no created being has any right over the Creator. Explanation: This is the answer of Imam Abu Yusuf, and the previous answer is better than this, the essence of which is that the hadith is not worthy of being used as evidence. Then this practice of saying in supplication 'by the right of so-and-so' is disliked (makruh) because no one has any right over Allah; rather, whatever He gives is pure grace. So contemplate. Warning: In [al-Sakb] al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 485, it is said that its occurrence is frequent. So let it be remembered. But if 'right' (haqq) is not taken in the sense to which the mind immediately turns, but rather by it is meant honor and greatness, or it is taken to mean 'means' (wasilah), then there is no harm in it. And in the lineages (shajars) of our mashayikh where it is used, it is only in the sense of tawassul, and wasilah is permissible. Allamah Shami, in Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 5, p. 254, indicated this interpretation and then said that all such probabilities are contrary to the apparent meaning; for this reason, our imams have absolutely prohibited it. I (the author) say: But using it in our language in the sense of tawassul is apparent, so the ruling of dislike will not apply, especially since it is supported by a hadith. The hadith is: 'O Allah, I ask You by the right of those who ask of You and by the right of my walking to You.' (Hadith in Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 5, p. 254).
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of saying 'bi haqqi fulan' (by the right of so-and-so) in supplication. It begins by presenting Imam Abu Yusuf's argument that no created being has a right over Allah, so such phrasing is makruh. The commentator then notes that if the word 'haqq' is interpreted as 'wasilah' (means) or honor, it becomes permissible, citing that the mashayikh use it only in the sense of tawassul. Allamah Shami warns that such interpretations contradict the apparent meaning, so the imams absolutely forbade it. However, the author (the commentator of Ashraf al-Hidayah) argues that in Urdu, the phrase is understood as tawassul, so the ruling of karahah does not apply, and he supports this with a hadith where the Prophet himself used similar wording. This reflects a nuanced Hanafi approach: the ruling is makruh based on the literal meaning, but ta'wil (interpretation) can remove the dislike if the wording is understood differently.

Key Terms
حق (haqq): Right or due; in this context, the literal meaning is a claim that obliges Allah, which is impossible for creatures.
توسل (tawassul): Seeking nearness to Allah through a means; here it refers to using the honor of pious individuals as a plea in dua.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the Hanafi imams considered saying 'bi haqqi fulan' as makruh?
A) It is an innovation in worship.
B) It implies a right over Allah, which no creature has.
C) It resembles Christian prayers.
D) It distracts from proper supplication.

Key Takeaway
Saying 'bi haqqi fulan' in dua is makruh if understood literally, but becomes permissible when interpreted as tawassul (seeking through honor).

Ruling on Chess, Backgammon, and Similar Games: Hanafi Position and Proof
Inter-madhhab dispute with Hanafi proof and intra-Hanafi difference on greeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on chess/backgammon, identify the proofs (hadith and principle of maysir), and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Playing chess/backgammon is either haram (if gambling) or makruh tahrimi (if idle play); distraction from worship makes it maysir.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position on games like chess and backgammon. It not only states the ruling but provides scriptural proof and addresses an opposing view attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i. You will also learn about the impact on a player's moral uprightness and a subtle intra-Hanafi difference on greeting such players.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State that the text from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir rules these games as makruh. However, the reasoning shows that if they involve gambling, they become haram (maysir). If played without stakes, they are idle play (lahw) which is also prohibited unless within the three exceptions.
The ruling is conditional: makruh in absence of stakes, haram if stakes or distraction from worship.
2
Examine the two proofs
The first proof is a hadith that compares playing chess/backgammon to dipping hands in pig's blood, indicating severe prohibition. The second proof is the principle that anything distracting from Allah's remembrance and congregational prayers is maysir, citing a hadith.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, but still carries weight.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school (as narrated) permits chess because it sharpens the intellect. The Hanafi response: the textual proofs outweigh this benefit, and even without gambling, it is idle play.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is stronger due to explicit hadith.
4
Consider the effect on 'adalah
If the player gambles, his moral uprightness ('adalah) falls, making his testimony invalid. If he does not gamble, his 'adalah remains because he has a ta'wil (plausible interpretation) that the game is not harmful.
Ta'wil here refers to the player's belief that the game is permissible, which preserves his uprightness.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on greeting
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad dislike greeting chess players to deter them from the activity. Abu Hanifah permits greeting, reasoning that the interruption may distract them from the game.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi may depend on context.

قال ويكره اللعب بالشطرنج والنردو الاربعة عشر وكل لهو لانه ان قامر بها فالميسر حرام بالنص وهو اسم لكل قمار وان لم يقامر بها فهو عبث ولهو وقال عليه السلام لهو المؤمن باطل الا الثلاث تاديبه لفرسه ومناضلته عن قوسه وملاعبته مع اهله

ترجمه امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور شطرنج اور نرد اور چودہ گوئی کھیلنا مکروہ ہے اور ہر کھیل ( مکروہ ہے ) اسلئے کہ اگر اس نے ان سے جوا کھیلا تو جو احرام ہے نص کے ساتھ اور میسر نام ہے ہر جوئے کا اور اگر جوا نہ کھیلا تو یہ عبث اور لہو ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا مؤمن کا کھیل باطل ہے مگر تین ، اس کا اپنے گھوڑے کو ادب دینا، اور اپنی کمان سے تیر پھینکنا اور اس کی ملاعبت اپنی بیوی سے۔ تشریح شطرنج اور نرد اور چودہ گوئی اور ایسے جملہ قسم کے کھیل مکروہ ہیں کیونکہ اگر ان کھیلوں میں جوئے کا پہلو ہو تو اسکی حرمت نص سے ثابت ہے اور اگر جوتے کا پہلو نہ ہوتو یہ سارے کھیل عبث واغو کام میں جو حرام ہے اور حدیث میں مؤمن کے تمام کھیلوں کو باطل کہا ہے علاوہ تین کے۔

ا شه سواری -۲- تیراندازی اپنی بیوی سے ملاعبت

بعض حضرات کا مسلک

وقال بعض الناس يباح اللعب بالشطرنج لما فيه من تشحيذ الخواطر وتذكية الافهام وهو محكى عن الشافعي

ترجمہ اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ شطرنج کھیلنا مباح ہے اسلئے کہ اسمیں ذہنوں کو تیز کرنا اور افہام و تیز کرتا ہے۔ اور یہی منقول ہے شافعی ہے۔ تشریح بعض حضرات نے شطرنج کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اسلئے کہ اس میں ذہن تیز اور چوکس ہوتا ہے امام شافعی سے بھی یہی منقول ہے۔ احناف کی دلیل

ولنا قوله عليه السلام من لعب بالشطرنج والنرد شير فكانما غمس يده فى دم الخنزير ولا نه نوع لعب

۳۹۳ كتاب الكراهية اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ يصد عن ذكر الله وعن الجمع والجماعات فيكون حراما لقوله عليه السلام ما الهاك عن ذكر الله فهو میسر ثم ان قامر به تسقط عدالته وان لم يقامر لا تسقط لانه متاول فيه وكره ابو يوسف ومحمد التسليم عليهم تحذيراً لهم ولم ير ابو حنيفة به باسا ليشغلهم عملهم فيه

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل فرمان نبی علیہ السلام ہے جو شطرنج اور نردشیر کھیلا تو گویا اس نے اپنا ہاتھ خنزیر کے خون میں ڈبویا اور اسلئے کہ یہ کھیل کی ایسی قسم ہے جو اللہ کے ذکر سے روکتی ہے اور جمعوں اور جماعتوں سے روکتی ہے تو یہ حرام ہوگا نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے، جس کام نے تجھ کو اللہ کے ذکر سے غافل کر دیا تو وہ جوا ہے پھر اگر اس نے کھیل سے جوا کھیلا تو اس کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اگر جوا نہ کھیلا تو ساقط نہیں ہوگی اسلئے کہ وہ اس میں تاویل کرنے والا ہے اور ابو یوسف و محمدؐ نے ان پر سلام کرنے کو مکروہ جانا ہے ان کی تحذیر کی غرض سے اور ابو حنیفہ نے اس میں کوئی جرم نہیں سمجھا تا کہ ان کو اس سے مشغول کر دے جس میں وہ ہیں۔

تشریح ہم نے ان کھیلیوں کو مکروہ قرار دیا ہے جس کی دلیل مذکور ہوئی پھر یہ تمام کھیل جمعہ اور جماعات اور اللہ کے ذکر سے غافل کرتے ہیں لہذا ان کا بنص حدیث جوا ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے پھر ان کھیلوں میں مبتلا ہونے والا جوا باز بھی ہو تو اس کا عادل ہو نا ختم ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اس کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہوگی اور اگر جوا بازی اور سٹہ بازی نہ کرے تو ساقط العدالت نہ ہو گا۔ پھر صاحبین نے تو ایسے لوگوں کو سلام کرنا مکروہ قرار دیا ہے تا کہ ان کو کچھ تنبیہ ہو لیکن امام صاحب نے سلام کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور دلیل یہ دی ہے کہ جتنی دیر سلام اور اسکے جواب میں خرچ ہوگی اتنی دیر تک یہ لوگ کھیل سے باز آئیں گے۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Playing chess, backgammon, and 'fourteen' is disliked (makruh), and every vain game, because if he gambles with them, then gambling is haram by the text (of Quran), and 'maysir' is the name for every gambling; and if he does not gamble, then it is idle play and vain. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The play of a believer is vain except three: training his horse, shooting his bow, and playing with his wife.' Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Playing chess, backgammon, and 'fourteen' is makruh, and every game (is makruh) because if he gambles with them, then gambling is haram by the text, and maysir is the name for every gambling; and if he does not gamble, then it is idle play and vain. The Prophet said: 'The play of a believer is vain except three: training his horse, shooting his bow, and playing with his wife.' Explanation: Chess, backgammon, 'fourteen', and all such games are makruh because if they involve gambling, their prohibition is established by the text; and if they do not involve gambling, they are idle play and vain, which is haram. And in the hadith, all plays of a believer are called vain except three: horse riding, archery, and playing with one's wife. The stance of some people: And some people said that playing chess is permissible because it sharpens the mind and stimulates intelligence, and this is narrated from al-Shafi'i. Translation: And some people said that playing chess is mubah because it sharpens the intellect and stimulates understanding. And this is narrated from al-Shafi'i. Explanation: Some people declared chess permissible because it sharpens the mind, and this is also narrated from Imam al-Shafi'i. The proof of the Hanafis: And we have the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever plays chess and backgammon, it is as if he dipped his hand in the blood of a pig.' And because it is a type of play that prevents from the remembrance of Allah and from the congregational prayers, so it is haram due to the saying of the Prophet: 'Whatever distracts you from the remembrance of Allah is maysir.' Then, if he gambles with it, his uprightness ('adalah) falls; and if he does not gamble, it does not fall because he is engaged in ta'wil (interpretation). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disliked greeting them as a deterrent, but Abu Hanifah saw no harm in it to engage them in their activity. Translation: And our proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'Whoever plays chess and backgammon, it is as if he dipped his hand in the blood of a pig.' And because this game is of a type that prevents from the remembrance of Allah and from the congregations, so it will be haram due to the saying of the Prophet: 'Whatever distracts you from the remembrance of Allah is maysir.' Then if he gambles with it, his 'adalah falls; if he does not gamble, it does not fall because he is engaged in ta'wil. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disliked greeting them as a deterrent, and Abu Hanifah saw no harm in it so that they may be occupied in their activity. Explanation: We have declared these games makruh, as the proof mentioned. Then all these games distract from Friday prayer, congregations, and remembrance of Allah, so they are proven to be maysir by the text of the hadith. Then if the player gambles, his being upright ends—i.e., his testimony is not accepted; and if he does not gamble, his uprightness does not fall. Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disliked greeting such people as a deterrent, but Imam (Abu Hanifah) permitted greeting, reasoning that the time spent in greeting and responding will keep them away from the game.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute with intra-Hanafi differences on the ruling of chess, backgammon, and similar games. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir: playing chess, backgammon, and 'fourteen' is makruh. The reason is twofold: if played for stakes, it is haram as gambling (maysir); if not, it is idle play (lahw) which is also prohibited because the Prophet said a believer's play is vain except three specific activities (horse training, archery, and playing with one's wife). The commentator explains that all such games are makruh. Then the passage presents the opposing view: some (attributed to al-Shafi'i) permit chess because it sharpens the mind. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: (1) a hadith that likens playing chess/backgammon to dipping hands in pig's blood (a strong condemnation), and (2) the principle that anything distracting from Allah's remembrance is maysir (gambling). The passage also discusses the effect on the player's moral uprightness ('adalah): if he gambles, his testimony becomes invalid; if not, his uprightness remains because he has a ta'wil (plausible interpretation) for playing. Finally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad dislike greeting such players to deter them, while Abu Hanifah permits greeting to distract them from the game. This shows the Hanafi school's nuanced approach: the ruling is makruh, but with considerations of context and intent.

Key Terms
شطرنج (shatranj): A board game played with pieces representing royal figures; derived from Sanskrit 'chaturanga'.
نرد (nard): Backgammon; a dice game invented by Ardashir ibn Babak.
ميسر (maysir): A pre-Islamic game of chance; in fiqh, it refers to any gambling contract.
قمار (qimar): Gambling; any game where one party gains at the expense of another through chance.
عدالت ('adalah): Moral uprightness required for a witness's testimony to be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, what happens to the 'adalah (uprightness) of a person who plays chess without gambling?
A) It is automatically nullified
B) It remains intact because of ta'wil
C) It becomes invalid only if he plays with non-Muslims
D) It is permanently lost

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views chess/backgammon as prohibited (makruh tahrimi) unless played without stakes and without distraction from religious duties, and the player's uprightness is only affected if gambling occurs.

Hanafi Rulings on Games: Permissible and Impermissible
Summarizes Hanafi rules on various games including gambling definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on games, distinguishing permissible from impermissible, and identify when games become gambling (maysir/tamar).

Core Idea
Games with no benefit are haram; beneficial games are halal without stakes; any stake turns a game into haram gambling.

This lesson distills the Hanafi principles on recreational games from a series of warnings (tanbeehat) in Jawahir al-Fiqh. The passage lists various impermissible games and establishes a clear test: any game lacking a legitimate religious or worldly benefit is prohibited, while beneficial games are permissible only when played without stakes. Understanding this framework is essential for navigating modern sports and pastimes within Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of games
Read the passage and note that games are divided into those with no significant benefit (impermissible) and those with benefit (permissible with conditions).
The passage explicitly lists examples like pigeon flying and cock fighting as impermissible, and ball games and wrestling as permissible.
2
Extract the condition for permissible games
Observe that permissible games must be played with a beneficial intention and may not involve any stakes or prize conditions.
Even beneficial games become haram if stakes are attached, as that constitutes tamar/maysir.
3
Define gambling (maysir/tamar)
The passage defines any transaction ambiguous between profit and loss as tamar/maysir (gambling), which is haram.
This definition covers all forms of betting and prize competitions beyond the excepted cases of horse racing and archery.
4
Apply the principle to modern examples
Use the principles to classify common modern games: football for exercise (halal if no stakes), chess for mental skill (halal if no stakes), card games for pure fun (haram).
The intention and presence of stakes are decisive factors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ شطرنج بشین کے کسرہ کے ساتھ ایک کھیل جو ہندوستان وغیرہ میں مشہور ہے یہ مسکرت کا لفظ ہے جو اصل میں چترنگ ہے معرب ہے اس میں چھ قسم کے مہروں سے کھیلتے ہیں جو شاہ، فرزین، فیل، اسپ، رخ اور پیدل کہلاتے ہیں ، شامی نے کہا ہے کہ یہ شدر نج کا مغرب ہے ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۲۵۳ ج ۵ ۔ نرداور نردشیر یہ فارسی سے معرب ہے یہ ایک کھیل ہے جس کو اردشیر بن بابک نے ایجاد کیا ہے اس لئے اس کونر دشیر کہتے ہیں قہستانی میں ہے کہ یہ کھیل شاپور بن اردشیر کی موضوعات میں سے ہے جو ملوک ساسانیہ کا دوسرا بادشاہ ہے۔ وهو حرام شامی ص ۲۵۳ ج ۵ اربعة عشر چودہ گوئی کا ایک کھیل ہے جو حرام ہے۔

تنبیہ - باب کی پہلی حدیث کو اصحاب سنن نے نقل کیا ہے اور دوسری حدیث بایں الفاظ غریب ہے مسلم میں یہ حدیث ہے لیکن اس میں شطرنج کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ تیسری حدیث بایں الفاظ غریب ہے۔ تنبیہ - ایسے کھیل تماشے جن کے تحت میں کوئی معتد بہا فائدہ دین و دنیا کا نہ ہو وہ سب ممنوع اور نا جائز ہیں خواہ ان پر بازی لگائی جائے یا انفرادی طور پر کھیلا جائے لہذا کبوتر بازی ، پتنگ باری، بٹیر بازی ، مرغ ،بازی ، چوسر ، شطرنج، تاش ، کتوں کی ریس وغیرہ سب اسی نا جائز صورت کے افراد ہیں۔ جواہر الفقہ ص ۲۵۳ ج ۲

تنبیه - جن کھیلوں سے کچھ دینی یا دنیوی فوائد حاصل ہو سکتے ہوں وہ جائز ہیں۔ بشرطیکہ انہیں فوائد کی نیت سے ان کو کھیلا جائے محض لہو و لعب کی نیت نہ ہو لیکن اس کی بازی پر کوئی معارضہ یا انعام شرط مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں ، مثلاً گیند کا کھیل کہ اس سے جسمانی ورزش بنتی ہے اور ہوتی ہے لہذا والی بال ، فیٹ بال سب جائز ہیں ) یا لاٹھی وغیرہ کے کھیل، یا پہلوانوں کی کشتی وغیرہ جو قوت جہاد میں معین ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح معمہ بازی شعر بازی تعلیمی تاش، ہار جیت کی بازی لگانا، مگر اس پر کوئی رقم معاوضہ کی مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں بلکہ تمار حرام ہے۔ جواہر الفقہ ص ۲۵۱ ج۲ تنبیہ - ہر وہ معاملہ جو نفع اور نقصان کے درمیان مبہم ہو اصطلاح شرع میں تمار اور میسر کہلاتا ہے اردوزبان میں اسکو جوا کہا جاتا ہے۔
Warning: Chess, with a kasra on the shin, is a game famous in India etc. It is an Arabicized word, originally 'chaturanga'. It is played with six types of pieces called Shah, Farzin, Fil, Asp, Rukh, and Paidal. Shami said it is derived from 'shatranj', see Shami vol. 5 p. 253. Backgammon (nard and nardshir) is Arabicized from Persian. It is a game invented by Ardashir ibn Babak, thus called nardshir. Al-Qahustani says it is among the innovations of Shapur ibn Ardashir, the second king of the Sasanian dynasty. And it is haram, Shami vol. 5 p. 253. 'Fourteen' ('arba'ata 'ashar) is a game that is haram. Warning: The first hadith of the chapter is narrated by the authors of the Sunan; the second hadith is weak (gharib) in these words; Muslim has a hadith but without mention of chess. The third hadith is also gharib. Warning: Those games and spectacles that have no significant benefit for religion or worldly life are all prohibited, whether played for stakes or individually. Thus, pigeon flying, kite flying, quail fighting, cock fighting, chausar, chess, cards, dog racing, etc., are all instances of this impermissible category. (Jawahir al-Fiqh vol. 2 p. 253) Warning: Games from which some religious or worldly benefits can be obtained are permissible, provided they are played with the intention of those benefits, not merely for idle play. But on their game, no competition or prize condition may be set. For example, ball games which provide physical exercise, so volleyball, football are all permissible; or stick games, or wrestling games that help in jihad strength. Similarly, puzzle games, poetry games, educational cards, playing for winning or losing, but stipulating any monetary compensation is not permissible; rather, it is tamar (gambling) which is haram. (Jawahir al-Fiqh vol. 2 p. 251) Warning: Every transaction that is ambiguous between profit and loss is, in the terminology of Shari'ah, called tamar or maysir, and in Urdu it is called 'jua' (gambling).
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a series of warnings (tanbeehat) providing general principles on games. It first gives background on chess, backgammon, and 'fourteen', noting that chess is originally from India, and backgammon was invented by Persian kings. It refers to Shami and Qahustani for rulings. Then it lists various games that are impermissible (pigeon flying, kite flying, quail fights, etc.) because they have no significant benefit. It then states the principle: games with religious or worldly benefits are permissible if played with that intention, but no stakes are allowed; otherwise, it becomes gambling (tamar/maysir). Finally, it defines gambling as any ambiguous transaction where gain/loss is uncertain. This provides a comprehensive summary of Hanafi fiqh on recreational games.

Key Terms
ميسر (maysir): Any gambling transaction where gain or loss is uncertain; a term from pre-Islamic Arabia.
تمار (tamar): A type of gambling involving dice or lots; used synonymously with maysir.
عبث ('abath): Idle play or purposeless activity.
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess, often considered haram due to lack of benefit or connection to gambling; here listed among impermissible games.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is permissible (halal) if played with a beneficial intention but without stakes?
A) Pigeon flying
B) Cock fighting
C) Football (physical exercise)
D) Card playing with money

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of a game depends on its benefit and the presence of stakes; any stake turns a game into haram gambling.

Ruling on Chess and Backgammon and Greeting the Players
Ruling on chess/backgammon with hadith proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on greeting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on chess and backgammon, identify the hadith proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on greeting players.

Core Idea
Chess and backgammon are haram because they distract from dhikr and are akin to gambling; greeting players is disputed among Hanafi imams.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the legal status of popular board games and the etiquette of interacting with players. It establishes the prohibition based on prophetic hadith and then navigates a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding whether it is appropriate to greet those engaged in such games.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on two specific games: chess (shatranj) and backgammon (nardashir). Determine their legal status (hukm) according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is explicitly stated as haram (forbidden).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Whatever distracts you from remembrance of Allah is gambling.' Find this proof and note its authority (sunan, thubut zanni).
The hadith is a marfu' hadith transmitted by the compilers of the Sunan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The key phrase 'distracts from dhikr' includes the games, and the term 'maysir' (gambling) makes it haram.
The dalala (indication) is qati' (definitive) for the ruling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on greeting
The text records a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on the ruling of greeting players. Identify each position and their reasoning.
Abu Hanifa saw no harm; the Sahibayn considered it makruh as a deterrent.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference in daily life: whether to greet someone playing chess. This shows the flexibility within the madhhab.
Both opinions are recorded, and the mufta bihi is not explicitly stated, but Abu Hanifa's view is presented first.

Source Text

كتاب الكراهية اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ يصد عن ذكر الله وعن الجمع والجماعات فيكون حراما لقوله عليه السلام ما الهاك عن ذكر الله فهو میسر ثم ان قامر به تسقط عدالته وان لم يقامر لا تسقط لانه متاول فيه وكره ابو يوسف ومحمد التسليم عليهم تحذيراً لهم ولم ير ابو حنيفة به باسا ليشغلهم عملهم فيه
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل فرمان نبی علیہ السلام ہے جو شطرنج اور نردشیر کھیلا تو گویا اس نے اپنا ہاتھ خنزیر کے خون میں ڈبویا اور اسلئے کہ یہ کھیل کی ایسی قسم ہے جو اللہ کے ذکر سے روکتی ہے اور جمعوں اور جماعتوں سے روکتی ہے تو یہ حرام ہوگا نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے، جس کام نے تجھ کو اللہ کے ذکر سے غافل کر دیا تو وہ جوا ہے پھر اگر اس نے کھیل سے جوا کھیلا تو اس کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اگر جوا نہ کھیلا تو ساقط نہیں ہوگی اسلئے کہ وہ اس میں تاویل کرنے والا ہے اور ابو یوسف و محمدؐ نے ان پر سلام کرنے کو مکروہ جانا ہے ان کی تحذیر کی غرض سے اور ابو حنیفہ نے اس میں کوئی جرم نہیں سمجھا تا کہ ان کو اس سے مشغول کر دے جس میں وہ ہیں۔
تشریح ہم نے ان کھیلیوں کو مکروہ قرار دیا ہے جس کی دلیل مذکور ہوئی پھر یہ تمام کھیل جمعہ اور جماعات اور اللہ کے ذکر سے غافل کرتے ہیں لہذا ان کا بنص حدیث جوا ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے پھر ان کھیلوں میں مبتلا ہونے والا جوا باز بھی ہو تو اس کا عادل ہو نا ختم ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اس کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہوگی اور اگر جوا بازی اور سٹہ بازی نہ کرے تو ساقط العدالت نہ ہو گا۔ پھر صاحبین نے تو ایسے لوگوں کو سلام کرنا مکروہ قرار دیا ہے تا کہ ان کو کچھ تنبیہ ہو لیکن امام صاحب نے سلام کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور دلیل یہ دی ہے کہ جتنی دیر سلام اور اسکے جواب میں خرچ ہوگی اتنی دیر تک یہ لوگ کھیل سے باز آئیں گے۔
تنبیہ شطرنج بشین کے کسرہ کے ساتھ ایک کھیل جو ہندوستان وغیرہ میں مشہور ہے یہ مسکرت کا لفظ ہے جو اصل میں چترنگ ہے معرب ہے اس میں چھ قسم کے مہروں سے کھیلتے ہیں جو شاہ، فرزین، فیل، اسپ، رخ اور پیدل کہلاتے ہیں ، شامی نے کہا ہے کہ یہ شدر نج کا مغرب ہے ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۲۵۳ ج ۵ ۔ نرداور نردشیر یہ فارسی سے معرب ہے یہ ایک کھیل ہے جس کو اردشیر بن بابک نے ایجاد کیا ہے اس لئے اس کونر دشیر کہتے ہیں قہستانی میں ہے کہ یہ کھیل شاپور بن اردشیر کی موضوعات میں سے ہے جو ملوک ساسانیہ کا دوسرا بادشاہ ہے۔ وهو حرام شامی ص ۲۵۳ ج ۵ اربعة عشر چودہ گوئی کا ایک کھیل ہے جو حرام ہے۔
تنبیہ - باب کی پہلی حدیث کو اصحاب سنن نے نقل کیا ہے اور دوسری حدیث بایں الفاظ غریب ہے مسلم میں یہ حدیث ہے لیکن اس میں شطرنج کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ تیسری حدیث بایں الفاظ غریب ہے۔ تنبیہ - ایسے کھیل تماشے جن کے تحت میں کوئی معتد بہا فائدہ دین و دنیا کا نہ ہو وہ سب ممنوع اور نا جائز ہیں خواہ ان پر بازی لگائی جائے یا انفرادی طور پر کھیلا جائے لہذا کبوتر بازی ، پتنگ باری، بٹیر بازی ، مرغ ،بازی ، چوسر ، شطرنج، تاش ، کتوں کی ریس وغیرہ سب اسی نا جائز صورت کے افراد ہیں۔ جواہر الفقہ ص ۲۵۳ ج ۲
تنبیه - جن کھیلوں سے کچھ دینی یا دنیوی فوائد حاصل ہو سکتے ہوں وہ جائز ہیں۔ بشرطیکہ انہیں فوائد کی نیت سے ان کو کھیلا جائے محض لہو و لعب کی نیت نہ ہو لیکن اس کی بازی پر کوئی معارضہ یا انعام شرط مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں ، مثلاً گیند کا کھیل کہ اس سے جسمانی ورزش بنتی ہے اور ہوتی ہے لہذا والی بال ، فیٹ بال سب جائز ہیں ) یا لاٹھی وغیرہ کے کھیل، یا پہلوانوں کی کشتی وغیرہ جو قوت جہاد میں معین ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح معمہ بازی شعر بازی تعلیمی تاش، ہار جیت کی بازی لگانا، مگر اس پر کوئی رقم معاوضہ کی مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں بلکہ تمار حرام ہے۔ جواہر الفقہ ص ۲۵۱ ج۲ تنبیہ - ہر وہ معاملہ جو نفع اور نقصان کے درمیان مبہم ہو اصطلاح شرع میں تمار اور میسر کہلاتا ہے اردوزبان میں اسکو جوا کہا جاتا ہے۔
تنبیه شامی باب ما يفسد الصلوۃ میں ان مقامات کو بیان کیا گیا ہے جہاں سلام کرنا مکروہ ہے ان میں سے شطرنج کھیلنے والا بھی ہے نیز فاسق معلن کو سلام کرنا فقہاء نے مکروہ لکھا ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب محمد یوسف غفرلہ تا ؤلوی تنبیہ کے ڈاڑھی منڈانے والا اور مخفی رکھنے والا بھی فاسق معلن ہے قائدہ کے مطابق ان کو بھی سلام کرنا مکروہ ہے مگر حضرت مولانا اشرف علی تھانوی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان کو تعلیم کی غرض سے سلام کیا جا سکتا ہے نہ کہ تعظیم کی۔
Book of Disliked Things. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu Sharh Hidayah Vol 13. [He] distracts from remembrance of Allah and from congregations and Friday prayers, so it is forbidden because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whatever distracts you from remembrance of Allah is gambling.' Then if he gambles with it, his moral integrity (adala) is forfeited; if he does not gamble, it is not forfeited because he has a valid interpretation. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disliked greeting them as a warning to them. Abu Hanifa did not see any harm in it to occupy them from their activity. Translation: And our evidence is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever plays chess and backgammon, it is as if he dipped his hand in the blood of a pig.' And because this type of game prevents from remembrance of Allah and from congregations and Friday prayers, so it will be forbidden due to the Prophet's statement: 'Whatever distracts you from remembrance of Allah is gambling.' Then if he gambles through the game, his moral integrity (adala) is forfeited, meaning his testimony is not acceptable; if he does not gamble, he is not disqualified because he is engaged in interpretation (ta'wil). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with them) considered it disliked (makruh) to greet them as a deterrent, but Abu Hanifa saw no harm in it so that they would be distracted from their activity. Explanation: We have declared these games as disliked (makruh) due to the evidence mentioned. Then all these games distract from Friday prayers and congregations and from remembrance of Allah, so by the text of the hadith they are proven to be gambling. Then if the player is also a gambler, his moral integrity (adala) terminates, i.e., his testimony is not acceptable; if he does not gamble or bet, he is not disqualified. Then the two companions (Sahibayn) consider greeting such people as disliked to give them a warning, but the Imam (Abu Hanifa) considered greeting permissible with the evidence that the time spent in greeting and its response will keep them away from the game. Note: Chess (shatranj) with a kasra on the sheen is a game well-known in India etc. It is an Arabicized word from 'chaturang'. There are six types of pieces: king, minister, elephant, horse, chariot, and pawn. Al-Shami said it is an Arabized form of 'shatranj'. See Shami vol. 5 p. 253. Nard (backgammon) and nardashir are Arabicized from Persian; a game invented by Ardashir bin Babak, hence called nardashir. Qahistani says it is from the innovations of Shapur bin Ardashir, the second Sassanid king. It is forbidden (haram). Shami vol. 5 p. 253. Fourteen (game) is a forbidden game. Note: The first hadith of the chapter was transmitted by the compilers of the Sunan; the second hadith with these words is rare; Muslim has this hadith but does not mention chess. The third hadith with these words is rare. Note: Games and amusements that have no substantial benefit in religion or world are all prohibited and impermissible, whether played for stakes or individually. Thus pigeon-flying, kite-flying, quail-fighting, cock-fighting, backgammon, chess, cards, dog racing etc. are all instances of this impermissible category. (Jawahir al-Fiqh vol. 2 p. 253). Note: Games that have some religious or worldly benefit are permissible, provided they are played with the intention of such benefit, not merely for amusement. But it is not permissible to stipulate a prize or reward on the outcome. For example, ball games that provide physical exercise (volleyball, football), or stick games, or wrestling that aids jihad, etc. Similarly, riddles, poetry games, educational cards – winning and losing may occur, but no monetary compensation may be stipulated; otherwise it is gambling (qimar) which is haram. (Jawahir al-Fiqh vol. 2 p. 251). Note: Every transaction that is ambiguous between profit and loss is called gharar or maysir in Shariah, and in Urdu it is called gambling (juwa). Note: Al-Shami in the chapter on nullifiers of prayer mentions the places where greeting is disliked; among them is the chess player. Also greeting an open sinner (fasiq mu'lin) is considered disliked by the jurists. And Allah knows best what is correct. Muhammad Yusuf, may Allah forgive him. and the one who shaves his beard and conceals it is also an open sinner; according to the rule, greeting them is disliked. However, Hadrat Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi said that they may be greeted for the purpose of instruction, not as a sign of respect.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on chess and backgammon with proof from hadith and an intra-Hanafi dispute on greeting the players. It begins with the Arabic text from the Hidayah stating that chess and backgammon are haram because they distract from dhikr and from congregational prayers. The proof is the hadith: 'Whatever distracts you from remembrance of Allah is gambling.' The text then distinguishes between playing with and without gambling: if the player gambles, his testimony is rejected (saqitat al-adala); if not, his testimony remains valid because he may have a valid interpretation (ta'wil). This shows that playing without stakes is still haram but does not affect moral integrity. Then the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) consider it makruh to greet such players as a deterrent. Abu Hanifa sees no harm in greeting them because the time spent in greeting and response will distract them from the game. The commentary (tashrih) explains the reasoning and adds notes on other games, the definition of gambling (qimar), and the permissibility of beneficial games like sports. The final note (tanbih) from Shami clarifies that greeting chess players as well as open sinners is disliked, but Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi allows greeting for educational purposes.

Key Terms
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess, a game played with pieces, considered haram because it distracts from dhikr.
نردشير (nardashir): Backgammon, a game of dice, considered haram.
عدالت (adala): Moral integrity required for testimony; forfeited if one engages in gambling openly.
فاسق معلن (fasiq mu'lin): An open sinner who commits sin publicly without shame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on playing chess and backgammon?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahab)

Key Takeaway
Chess and backgammon are haram due to distraction from dhikr; greeting players is a matter of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Accepting Gifts from a Trading Slave: Between Qiyas and Istihsan
Ruling on gifts from trading slaves with istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting gifts from a trading slave and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas for small gifts.

Core Idea
Small gifts from a trading slave are lawful by necessity; valuable ones remain unlawful by strict analogy.

How should a Muslim respond when a slave engaged in trade offers a gift or invitation? Strict analogy would reject all such donations because the slave lacks full ownership. Yet the Hanafi school, drawing on the Prophet's own practice, makes a careful distinction: small items necessary for daily trade are permissible, while valuable gifts are disliked. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
From the passage, list each act (gift, invitation, borrowing mount, gift of clothes/money) and the ruling given (permissible vs. makruh).
The ruling is not uniform; it depends on the nature of the item.
2
Locate the qiyas and istihsan arguments
Note that the default ruling by qiyas is 'batil' (invalid) because the slave cannot make donations. Istihsan then overrides this for certain cases.
Understanding the tension between qiyas and istihsan is key.
3
Examine the dalil (Sunnah evidence)
Read the hadith cited: the Prophet accepted gifts from Salman (a slave) and Barirah (a mukatabah), and Companions accepted an invitation from a slave.
This provides the basis for istihsan.
4
Understand the concept of darura (necessity)
The passage argues that traders need small exchanges; necessity justifies departure from qiyas. Identify why this necessity applies to mounts and invitations but not to clothes or money.
Necessity is the limiting factor.
5
Apply the distinction between small needs and valuables
Synthesize: the slave is authorized (ma'dhun), the item must be a common necessity of trade; otherwise the original qiyas holds.
This produces the two-tier ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تاجر غلام کا ہدیہ، دعوت قبول کرنے کا حکم، چوپاؤں کے عاریہ کا حکم ، غلام سے ہدیہ میں کپڑے، درا ہم ودنا نیر قبول کرنے کا حکم
قال ولا بأس بقبول هدية العبد التاجر واجابة دعوته واستعارة دابته وتكره كسوته الثوب وهديته الدراهم والدنانير وهذا استحسان وفى القياس كل ذلك باطل لانه تبرع والعبد ليس من اهله ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور تاجر غلام کا ہدیہ قبول کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اس کی دعوت قبول کرنے میں اور اس کا چوپایہ مستعار لینے میں ۔ اور مکروہ ہے غلام کا کپڑا پہنانا اور اس کا ہدیہ کرنا، در اہم و دنا نبیر کا، اور یہ (اس کا ہدیہ وغیرہ قبول کرنا ) استحسان ہے اور قیاس میں یہ سب باطل ہے اسلئے کہ یہ تبرع ہے اور غلام تبرع کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر غلام ماذون لا فی التجارة ہو اور وہ ہلکا سا (معمولی) ہدیہ پیش کرے تو جائز ہے اسی طرح دعوت کر دے تو جائز ہے یا اس کا گھوڑ ا مستعار لینا جائز ہے لیکن اگر وہ غلام ہدیہ میں کپڑے یا در اہم ودنا نیر وغیرہ پیش کرے تو اس کا قبول کرنا مکروہ ہے اور پہلی صورت میں جو جواز ہے یہ استحسان کی رو سے ہے ورنہ قیا س سب باطل ہے کیونکہ غلام عدم ملک کی وجہ سے تبرع کا اہل نہیں ہے اور یہ سب تبرع ہے ۔
استحسانی دلیل
وجه الاستحسان انه عليه السلام قبل هدية سلمان رضى الله عنه حين كان عبدا وقبل هدية بريرة رضى الله عنها وكانت مكاتبة واجاب رهط من الصحابة رضى الله عنهم دعوة مولى ابى اسيد و كان عبدا ولان في هــذه الاشياء ضرورة لايجد التاجر بدا منها ومن ملک شئيا يملك ما هو من ضروراته ولا ضرورة في الكسوة واهداء الدراهم فبقى على اصل القياس
ترجمه استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے سلمان فارسی کا ہدیہ قبول فرمایا جبکہ وہ غلام تھے اور حضرت بریرہ کاہد یہ قبول فرمایا اور وہ مکاتب تھیں اور صحابہ کی ایک جماع نے ابو اسید کے غلام کی دعوت قبول کی اور وہ غلام تھے اور اسلئے کہ ان چیزوں میں ضرورت ہے تاجران سے کوئی چارہ نہیں پاتا اور جو کسی شی کا مالک ہوتا ہے تو وہ اس کے لوازمات کا مالک ہوتا ہے اور کپڑا دینے اور دراہم کا ہدیہ کرنے میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے تو وہ اصل قیاس پر باقی رہا۔ تشریح یہاں سے استحسان کی دلیل بیان کی جارہی ہے:۔
1- حضرت سلمان فارسی کے ہدیہ کو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قبول فرمایا اور وہ غلام تھے پھر صدیق اکبر نے ان کو خرید کر آزاد کر دیا۔ ۲- حضرت عائشہ نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے پوچھا کہ بریڈ پر لوگ صدقہ کر دیتے ہیں وہ اس میں سے ہمارے پاس بھی بھیج دیتی ہے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ اس کیلئے صدقہ ہے اور ہمارے لئے ہدیہ ہے۔ علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث کے کسی طریق میں مجھے یہ نہیں ملا کہ بریرہ اس وقت مکاتب تھی ، مصنف عبد الرزاق میں عروہ سے
The gift of a trading slave, the ruling on accepting his invitation, the ruling on borrowing his mount, and the ruling on accepting from a slave a gift of clothes, dirhams, and dinars. He (Imam Muhammad) said: There is no harm in accepting the gift of a trading slave, responding to his invitation, and borrowing his mount. But it is disliked (makruh) to dress him in a garment or to accept his gift of dirhams and dinars. This (the permission) is istihsan; by qiyas all of it is batil (invalid) because it is a donation (tabarru') and a slave is not legally capable of donations. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: There is no harm in accepting the gift of a trading slave, in responding to his invitation, and in borrowing his mount. And it is makruh to accept from a slave a garment or his gift of dirhams and dinars. This (accepting) is istihsan; by qiyas all of it is invalid because it is a donation and a slave is not qualified for donations. Explanation: If the slave is authorized to trade (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijara) and he offers a small gift, it is permissible; similarly if he offers an invitation or if one borrows his horse. But if the slave offers a garment or dirhams and dinars as a gift, accepting it is makruh. The permissibility in the first case is due to istihsan; otherwise, by qiyas, all is invalid because the slave, due to lack of ownership, is not qualified for donations. The istihsan evidence: The reason for istihsan is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the gift of Salman (may Allah be pleased with him) when he was a slave, and accepted the gift of Barirah (may Allah be pleased with her) when she was a mukatabah (slave with contract of manumission), and a group of Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) accepted the invitation of the slave of Abu Asid when he was a slave. And because in these things there is a necessity; the trader cannot do without them, and whoever owns something owns its necessities. But there is no necessity in giving clothes or gifting dirhams, so those remain on the original qiyas. Translation: The istihsan evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the gift of Salman al-Farsi while he was a slave, and accepted the gift of Sayyidah Barirah while she was a mukatabah, and a group of Companions accepted the invitation of the slave of Abu Asid while he was a slave. And because there is a necessity: traders cannot avoid these things. And whoever owns something owns its necessities. There is no necessity in giving clothes or gifting dirhams, so those remain on the original qiyas. Explanation: Here the istihsan evidence is being explained. 1- The Prophet accepted Salman's gift while he was a slave; later Abu Bakr purchased and freed him. 2- Sayyidah A'ishah asked the Prophet about Barirah: People give her charity and she sends some of it to us. The Prophet said: It is charity for her and a gift for us. Allamah Zayla'i says: I have not found in any chain of hadith that Barirah was a mukatabah at that time. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq from 'Urwa...)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on accepting gifts and other benefits from a trading slave (al-`abd al-tajir). It begins with a summary of the ruling: it is permissible (la ba's) to accept a gift from a trading slave, to respond to his invitation, and to borrow his mount. However, it is makruh (disliked) to accept a gift of clothing or money (dirhams/dinars) from him. This permissibility is based on istihsan (juristic preference), whereas the strict analogy (qiyas) would render all such donations invalid because a slave lacks full ownership and thus is not legally capable of making donations (tabarru'). The commentary clarifies that the slave must be authorized to trade (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijara). In that case, small gifts are permissible, but valuable items are makruh. The istihsan evidence is then cited: the Prophet accepted gifts from Salman (when he was a slave) and from Barirah (when she was a mukatabah), and the Companions accepted an invitation from a slave. The reasoning is that traders have a practical need for such exchanges; ownership of the slave's trade extends to its necessities. However, there is no necessity for giving clothes or money, so the original qiyas (invalidity) applies to those. The translation and additional commentary provide examples and note a point from Allamah Zayla'i regarding Barirah's status.

Key Terms
غلام مأذون (ghulam ma'dhun): A slave who is authorized by his master to engage in trade.
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous donation or gift without consideration.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to necessity, ease, or stronger evidence.
ضرورة (darura): Necessity that legitimizes departure from strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on accepting a gift of clothing from a trading slave?
A) Permissible (halal)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahab)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, accepting small gifts from a trading slave is permissible by istihsan due to necessity, but valuable gifts remain disliked (makruh) because qiyas renders them invalid.

Transactions on Minors: Classification and Authority
Classification of minor's transactions and ruling on foundling gifts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of tasarruf for minors and identify who is authorized for each type according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Transactions on minors are of three types: guardianship, necessity, and pure benefit — each with different authorized persons.

This passage introduces a foundational classification of legal transactions (tasarrufat) that can be performed on behalf of a minor. Understanding this classification is essential for determining who can validly act for a minor in matters like marriage, sale, purchase, and hiring. The text also specifically addresses the caretaker of a foundling (laqit) and his authority to accept gifts and charity. We will parse the three categories and their respective conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of tasarruf
The text states that transactions on minors are of three types. List them based on the Arabic: tasarruf al-wilayah, tasarruf al-darurah, and tasarruf al-naf' al-mahd (the third is mentioned but not fully explained).
The third type is partially cut off in the source; we will focus on the first two complete types.
2
Define each type and its scope
For each type, determine: What kind of transaction does it cover? Who is authorized to perform it? What conditions apply?
Refer to the commentary for definitions.
3
Apply the classification to the foundling (laqit)
The text begins with the ruling on accepting gifts for a foundling. Relate this to the classification: which type of tasarruf does it fall under?
Gift acceptance for a foundling is a tasarruf of necessity or pure benefit?
4
Differentiate between guardian (wali) and caretaker (multaqit)
Note that the multaqit is not a full wali; he can only perform certain types of transactions. Identify which types are exclusive to the wali and which are permissible for the caretaker.
The text explicitly says tasarruf al-wilayah is only for the wali.

The caretaker of a foundling can accept gift and charity on behalf of the foundling. He said: Whoever has in his care a foundling with no father, it is permissible for him to accept gift and charity for him. The basis of this is that transactions concerning minors are of three types. One type is that which falls under guardianship (wilayah); no one can do it except the guardian, such as marriage, purchase, and sale of property for preservation, because the guardian is the one who stands in his place by deputation of the Shariah. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: And a person who has in his care a foundling who has no father, it is permissible for him to accept gift and charity for the foundling. The principle is that transactions on minors are of three types. One type is from the category of wilayah; no one can do it except the guardian, who is the one who stands in his place by deputation of the Shariah. Explanation: If someone finds a newborn baby on the road and picks him up, that baby is a foundling (laqit). So if someone gives a gift or charity for that foundling, the caretaker can accept possession for him. Then transactions on minors are of three types: (1) Tasarruf al-wilayah, (2) Tasarruf al-darurah, (3) Tasarruf al-naf' al-mahd. In tasarruf al-wilayah, only the guardian (father, grandfather, paternal uncle, judge, etc.) is allowed to act, like contracting marriage, and buying and selling property that does not perish and is meant for preservation. Ruling on transactions and sale for minors. And another type is that which arises from the necessity of the minor's condition: purchasing what is indispensable for the minor, selling it, and hiring a wet nurse. This is permissible for the one who supports and spends on him, like the brother, paternal uncle, mother, and the caretake (multaqit) provided the child is in their care. And when these people have this type, the guardian is more entitled to it, except that it is not a condition for the guardian that the child be in his care. Translation: The second type is that which is from the necessity of the minor's condition: purchasing what is necessary for the minor, selling it, and hiring a wet nurse. This is permissible for the one who raises and spends on him, like the brother, uncle, mother, and caretake, provided the child is in their care. And when these people have this type, the guardian is more entitled, except that it is not a condition for the guardian that the child be in his care. Explanation: The second type is tasarruf al-darurah, i.e., buying necessary items for the minor or selling his goods if there is fear of damage, or hiring a wet nurse if the minor is an infant...
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage addresses the authority of the caretaker of a foundling (laqit) to accept gifts and charity on his behalf. It then introduces a foundational classification of transactions (tasarrufat) concerning minors into three types. The first type (tasarruf al-wilayah) is exclusive to the legal guardian (wali) — e.g., marriage, and sale/purchase of non-perishable assets for preservation. The second type (tasarruf al-darurah) is permissible for those who support the minor, such as close relatives or the multaqit (finder), for necessary purchases, sales, and hiring of a wet nurse, but the legal guardian has priority. The text begins to describe the third type (tasarruf al-naf' al-mahd) but is cut off at the end of the page. The classification is based on the capacity of the person dealing with the minor's property and the nature of the act.

Key Terms
لقیط (laqīṭ): A foundling; an abandoned child of unknown parentage.
تصرف (taṣarruf): Legal disposition or transaction involving a minor's property.
ولایت (wilāyah): Guardianship; legal authority to act on behalf of another.
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): Necessity; a condition that permits certain transactions for the minor's welfare.
نفع محض (naf' maḥḍ): Pure benefit; a transaction that is purely beneficial to the minor, with no loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Transactions on minors are classified into three types; only the legal guardian can perform guardianship transactions, while necessity transactions are open to supporters with care.

The Three Categories of Transactions for Foundlings and Minors
Classifies transactions over foundlings and minors into three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any transaction on behalf of a foundling or minor into one of the three categories (wilayah, darurah, naf' mahd) and state who is authorized to perform it.

Core Idea
Transactions on minors are governed by their benefit level: pure benefit opens to many, necessity to caregivers, and guardianship to the guardian alone.

This lesson from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the fundamental Hanafi framework for legal acts (tasarrufat) performed on behalf of foundlings (laqit) and minors. Imam Muhammad classifies all such acts into three types: those requiring exclusive guardianship, those permissible from necessity, and those of pure benefit. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly determining who can act for a minor in various transactions, from accepting gifts to selling property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act's category
Determine whether the act involves possible harm (wilayah), necessity for the minor's survival (darurah), or pure benefit (naf' mahd).
Wilayah acts include marriage and sale of property held for preservation; darurah includes buying essentials and hiring a wet nurse; naf' mahd includes accepting gifts and charity.
2
Apply the authority rule
For wilayah: only the legal guardian (father, grandfather, wasi, qadi) can act. For darurah: any person who supports and spends on the minor, provided the minor is in their care, can act. For naf' mahd: the finder, brother, uncle, and the minor himself (if discerning) can act.
The guardian also has authority for darurah and naf' mahd with priority.
3
Note the exception for guardians
For darurah, guardians have priority and do not require the minor to be under their care. For naf' mahd, the guardian can act without condition.
This flexibility ensures the minor is not deprived of benefits.
4
Contrast with other schools
Other schools may restrict these rights differently; the Hanafi position relies on the principle of benefit (maslahah) and the minimal risk in pure benefit acts.
This classification is unique to Hanafi fiqh.

خالص نفع ہے جیسے بہ قبول کرنا اور صدقہ قبول کرنا اور ان پر قبضہ کرنا تو ملتقط ، بھائی ، چا اور خود بچہ بھی یہ تصرف کر سکتا ہے جبکہ عاقل ہو اسلئے کہ حکمت کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ ایسا دروازہ کھولا جائے تا کہ بچہ کا فائدہ ہو تو عقل سے اور ولایت سے اور پرورش سے اس تصرف کی ولایت حاصل ہوگی بلکہ بغیر ولایت وحجر کے بھی اگر کوئی قبضہ کر کے بچہ کو دے تو صحیح ہے کیونکہ اس میں خالص نفع ہے اور یہ تو ایسا ہے جیسے بچہ پر خرچ کرنا تا کہ جس کا جتنا جی چاہے خرچ کر دے کیونکہ اس میں بچہ کا خالص نفع ہے۔ ملتقط یا چا کو یہ حق نہیں کہ بچہ کو اجارہ پر دے دیں قال ولا يجوز للملتقط ان يو اجره ويجوز للام ان تواجر ابنها اذا كان في حجرها ولا يجوز للعم لان الام تملک اتلاف منافعه باستخدامه ولا كذلك الملتقط والعم ولو اجر الصبى نفسه لا يجوز لانه مشوب بالضرر الا اذا فرغ من العمل لان عند ذلك تمحض نفعا فيجب المسى وهو نظير العبد المحجور يواجر نفسه وقد ذكرناه ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور ملتقط کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ لقیط کو اجارہ پر دے اور ماں کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے بیٹے کو اجارہ پر دے جبکہ وہ اس کی پرورش میں ہو اور چا کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ ماں اس کے منافع کو ضائع کرنے کی مالکہ ہے۔ اسے منفعت (خدمت) لے کر اور ملتقط اور چا ایسے نہیں ہیں اور اگر بچہ نے خود اپنے کو اجارہ پر دے دیا تو جائز نہیں اسلئے کہ یہ ضرر سے ملا ہوا ہے۔ مگر جبکہ وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس وقت میں محض نفع رہ گیا تو اجرت مسمی واجب ہوگی اور یہ غلام مجور کی نظیر ہے جو اپنے نفس کو اجارہ پر دے دے اور ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح متفقط یا چا وغیرہ کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ بچہ کو اجارہ پر دے دیں یعنی کسی کے یہاں اجیر وملازم رکھ دیں البتہ ماں کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ کسی کے یہاں اجیر و ملازم رکھ دے لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ بچہ ماں کی زیر پرورش ہو اسلئے کہ ماں کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ اپنے بیٹے سے
The one who has a foundling under his care can accept a gift or charity on the foundling's behalf. Imam Muhammad said: Whoever has a foundling with no father, it is permissible for him to accept a gift and charity for him. The basis of this is that transactions concerning minors are of three types: (1) That which falls under guardianship, which only a guardian can do, such as marriage, purchase, and sale of property that is kept for preservation, because the guardian is the one who stands in the place of the minor by appointment of the Sharia. (2) Another type is that which is necessary for the minor's situation, such as buying what is essential for the minor, selling his property, and hiring a wet nurse. This is permissible from the one who supports and spends on him, like the brother, uncle, mother, and finder, provided the minor is under their care. When these people have this authority, the guardian has it with priority, but for the guardian it is not a condition that the minor be under his care. (3) A third type is that which is pure benefit, like accepting a gift, charity, and taking possession. This is permissible for the finder, brother, uncle, and the minor himself if he is discerning, because wisdom dictates opening such a door for the minor's benefit. So he has authority by reason, guardianship, and custody, and it is like spending. Imam Muhammad said: It is not permissible for the finder to hire out the foundling, but it is permissible for the mother to hire out her son if he is under her care, and it is not permissible for the uncle, because the mother has the right to destroy his usufruct by utilizing him, unlike the finder and uncle. If the minor hires himself out, it is not permissible because it involves harm, unless he has completed the work, because then it becomes pure benefit, so the named wage becomes obligatory. This is analogous to the restricted slave who hires himself out.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the legal framework for transactions involving foundlings (laqīt) and minors under the Hanafi school. It opens by classifying actions (tasarrufāt) over minors into three categories. The first category is acts of guardianship (wilāyah) such as marriage and the sale of property held for preservation. Only the legal guardian (father, grandfather, executor, judge) can perform these. The second category is acts of necessity (ḍarūrah) like buying essential items, selling what is feared will spoil, or hiring a wet nurse. These can be performed by anyone who supports and spends on the minor (e.g., brother, uncle, mother, or finder) provided the minor is in their care. The guardian also has this authority with priority, but without the condition that the minor be under his care. The third category is acts of pure benefit (naf‘ maḥḍ) such as accepting a gift or charity and taking possession. Here the authority extends more widely: the finder, brother, uncle, and even the minor himself if he is discerning can act, because it is purely beneficial. The passage then addresses the specific issue of hiring out the minor (ijārah). The finder (multaqit) cannot hire out the foundling, nor can the uncle. However, the mother can hire out her son if he is under her care, because she has authority over his services. If the minor hires himself out, it is invalid during the work period due to potential harm, but after completion the wage is due as it becomes pure benefit. This is analogous to the restricted slave (ʿabd maḥjūr) who hires himself out.

Key Terms
لقيط (laqīṭ): A foundling, an abandoned child of unknown parentage taken into care.
تصرف (taṣarruf): A legal action or transaction, including buying, selling, accepting gifts, etc.
ولایت (wilāyah): Guardianship; legal authority to act on behalf of a minor in certain matters.
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of hire or lease, where a person's services are rented out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following is NOT an act of pure benefit (naf' mahd)?
A) Accepting a gift
B) Accepting charity
C) Selling property held for preservation
D) Taking possession of a gift

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes three levels of transactions on behalf of minors, each with its own set of authorized actors based on the degree of benefit and potential harm.

8 min
Rulings on Hiring Out a Foundling or Minor
Specific rulings on hiring out a foundling or minor and the analogy to the restricted slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who can hire out a foundling or minor, explain the rationale based on authority over usufruct, and apply the analogy to the restricted slave.

Core Idea
The right to hire out a minor follows the right to utilize his usufruct; only the mother has it, while the finder and uncle do not.

This lesson continues from the previous framework, focusing on the specific issue of hiring out (ijarah) a foundling or minor. Imam Muhammad rules that the finder (multaqit) and uncle cannot hire out the child, but the mother can. The minor himself cannot validly hire out his own services during the work period. An analogy is drawn to the restricted slave (abd mahjur) who hires himself out, illustrating the principle that acts mixed with harm are invalid until the harm is removed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor
Determine who is attempting to hire out the minor: finder, mother, uncle, or the minor himself.
The text explicitly address each of these.
2
Apply the ruling
Finder and uncle: not allowed. Mother (if child under her care): allowed. Minor himself: not allowed during work, but wage becomes due after completion.
The mother's authority is conditioned on the child being under her care.
3
Understand the underlying reason
The mother has the right to 'destroy' (tazlif) the child's usufruct, i.e., she can utilize his services without compensation, so she can also hire him out. The finder and uncle lack this right.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the mother has a unique authority over the child's labor.
4
Analyze the analogy
The minor hiring himself is like a restricted slave doing the same: both involve potential harm mixed with benefit, so the contract is invalid during the work period (due to potential harm), but after completion the wage becomes due (pure benefit remains).
The illa (effective cause) is the mixture of harm and benefit.

The third category is acts of pure benefit (naf‘ maḥḍ) such as accepting a gift or charity and taking possession. Here the authority extends more widely: the finder, brother, uncle, and even the minor himself if he is discerning can act, because it is purely beneficial. The passage then addresses the specific issue of hiring out the minor (ijārah). The finder (multaqit) cannot hire out the foundling, nor can the uncle. However, the mother can hire out her son if he is under her care, because she has authority over his services. If the minor hires himself out, it is invalid during the work period due to potential harm, but after completion the wage is due as it becomes pure benefit. This is analogous to the restricted slave (ʿabd maḥjūr) who hires himself out.

Key Terms
لقيط (laqīṭ): A foundling, an abandoned child of unknown parentage taken into care.
تصرف (taṣarruf): A legal action or transaction, including buying, selling, accepting gifts, etc.
ولایت (wilāyah): Guardianship; legal authority to act on behalf of a minor in certain matters.
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of hire or lease, where a person's services are rented out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a minor hires himself out for work?
A) The contract is valid and binding.
B) It is invalid entirely with no wage due.
C) It is invalid during work but the wage becomes due after completion.
D) It is valid if the guardian approves.

Key Takeaway
The right to hire out a minor is tied to the authority over usufruct; in the Hanafi school, only the mother enjoys this right, while others are excluded to protect the minor from potential harm.

Acts of Pure Benefit for an Orphan (Naf' Mahḍ)
Ruling on who may accept purely beneficial gifts and charity for an orphan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which acts qualify as naf' mahḍ and list the individuals authorized to perform them on behalf of an orphan according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Pure benefit opens the door: even the orphan himself can accept, no guardian needed.

A key principle in Hanafi fiqh is that certain acts like accepting gifts and charity are purely beneficial and involve no risk or harm. For an orphan child, the law expands the circle of those who can carry out such acts, going beyond the legal guardian to include the finder (multaqit), relatives, and even the child himself if he has some understanding. This lesson unpacks that rule and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify acts of pure benefit
Label acts like accepting a gift or charity as naf' mahḍ (purely beneficial). These are distinguished from acts that mix benefit and harm and require a guardian.
The text mentions qabūl (acceptance) and qabḍ (taking possession).
2
List authorized persons
From the text: the multaqit (finder), the brother, the paternal uncle, and the child himself if he is discerning (i.e., has some understanding).
Others like the mother are not listed; only these specified persons.
3
Understand the basis of authority
The child's own intellect (if he understands), the guardian's guardianship (wilāyah), and the custodian's custody (ḥaḍānah) each give authority to perform the act.
The multaqit's authority is debated but Hanafis grant it.
4
Appreciate the wisdom
The ruling is grounded in maṣlaḥah (public interest) for the orphan: opening the door for benefit without formal restrictions.
This is a qiyās on spending (infāq) on the orphan, which anyone can do.

And a third type: what is purely beneficial, like accepting a gift and charity and taking possession, then the finder (multaqit), the brother, the uncle, and the child himself (if he is discerning) own it, because what is suitable to wisdom is to open its door for the sake of the child. So he owns it by intellect (the child himself) and by guardianship (the guardian) and by custody (the one who raises him), and it became like spending.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding acts that are purely beneficial for an orphan child. The ruling is that the following individuals may perform such acts (accepting gifts, charity, and taking possession): the person who found the child (multaqit), the child's brother, the child's uncle, and even the child himself if he is discerning (i.e., has reached an age of understanding, typically around seven years). The reasoning is that wisdom requires opening the door for benefit to reach the child. The authority for these individuals comes from different sources: the child has it by his own intellect, the guardian by his guardianship, and the custodian by his custody. The commentator adds that even without formal guardianship or custody, if someone takes possession and gives it to the child, it is valid because it is purely beneficial, just like spending on the child.

Key Terms
ملتقط (multaqit): The person who finds and picks up an abandoned child (laqīṭ). He does not become a full guardian but has certain custodial rights.
نفع محض (naf' mahḍ): A purely beneficial act with no element of harm or risk, such as accepting a gift or charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the legal guardian (wali)
B) The multaqit (finder), brother, uncle, and the child if discerning
C) Only the qadi (judge)
D) Only the mother

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, acts of pure benefit (naf' mahd) for an orphan can be performed by the multaqit, relatives, and even the discerning child himself, not only the legal guardian.

Ruling on Hiring Out an Orphan Child: Who Has the Right?
Ruling with proof via qiyas on hiring orphan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which persons may validly hire out an orphan child and explain when a child's own hiring contract becomes enforceable according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mother can hire out her orphan child; the finder and uncle cannot. The child's own contract is initially void but becomes valid upon completion of work by istihsan.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the limits of guardianship over an orphan child with respect to hiring (ijārah). Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishes between those who have authority over the child's benefits and those who do not. The ruling also addresses a subtle case: when the child himself enters a hiring contract, which is normally invalid due to the mix of benefit and harm, but by istihsan becomes valid once the work is done, analogous to a restricted slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify who can hire out the orphan
List the persons mentioned: mother, multaqit (finder), uncle, and later additions: father, grandfather, qadi. Determine which are allowed and why.
Mother is allowed because she owns the right to use the child's benefits (manāfi'). Multaqit and uncle do not own this right.
2
Understand the reasoning for the mother's permission
The mother has a higher right over her child's benefits (istīmār) even to the extent of wasting them (atlāf). Therefore she can transfer that right to a third party via hire.
This is unique to the mother; the multaqit only has custodianship (ḥaḍānah), not ownership of benefits.
3
Analyze the child's own hiring contract
The child's contract is initially invalid because it combines benefit (wage) and harm (loss of freedom/service). But once the work is completed, the harm is removed and only benefit remains, so by istihsan the contract is validated and the named wage (musammā) becomes due.
The analogy is with a restricted slave (ʿabd maḥjūr) who hires himself out: also initially invalid but validated after work.
4
Apply the qiyas reasoning
The original case (aṣl) is the restricted slave; the new case (farʿ) is the orphan child. The common effective cause (ʿillah) is that the contract initially involves both benefit and harm, but after completion it becomes purely beneficial.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the text.
5
Note the addition from Ibn ʿAbidin
The commentator adds that father, grandfather, and the qadi also have the right to hire out the orphan. This is a later clarification from al-Shami.
This expands the ruling beyond the original text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملتقط یا چا کو یہ حق نہیں کہ بچہ کو اجارہ پر دے دیں
قال ولا يجوز للملتقط ان يو اجره ويجوز للام ان تواجر ابنها اذا كان في حجرها ولا يجوز للعم لان الام تملک اتلاف منافعه باستخدامه ولا كذلك الملتقط والعم ولو اجر الصبى نفسه لا يجوز لانه مشوب بالضرر الا اذا فرغ من العمل لان عند ذلك تمحض نفعا فيجب المسى وهو نظير العبد المحجور يواجر نفسه وقد ذكرناه
ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور ملتقط کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ لقیط کو اجارہ پر دے اور ماں کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے بیٹے کو اجارہ پر دے جبکہ وہ اس کی پرورش میں ہو اور چا کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ ماں اس کے منافع کو ضائع کرنے کی مالکہ ہے۔ اسے منفعت (خدمت) لے کر اور ملتقط اور چا ایسے نہیں ہیں اور اگر بچہ نے خود اپنے کو اجارہ پر دے دیا تو جائز نہیں اسلئے کہ یہ ضرر سے ملا ہوا ہے۔ مگر جبکہ وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس وقت میں محض نفع رہ گیا تو اجرت مسمی واجب ہوگی اور یہ غلام مجور کی نظیر ہے جو اپنے نفس کو اجارہ پر دے دے اور ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح متفقط یا چا وغیرہ کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ بچہ کو اجارہ پر دے دیں یعنی کسی کے یہاں اجیر وملازم رکھ دیں البتہ ماں کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ کسی کے یہاں اجیر و ملازم رکھ دے لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ بچہ ماں کی زیر پرورش ہو اسلئے کہ ماں کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ اپنے بیٹے سے منفعت خدمت لے کر اس کے منافع کو ضائع کر دے اور ملتقط اور چچا کو یہ حق نہیں ہے تو ان کو اجارہ پر بھی دینے کا حق نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر بچ نے خود اپنے آپ کو کہیں ملازم واجبیر ہونے کیلئے پیش کر دیا ہو تو یہ عقلاً جائز نہ ہو گا لیکن جب بچہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا کیونکہ بچہ کا عقد وہی سیح ہوتا ہے جو خالص نفع ہو اور یہاں نفع اور ضر ملا ہوا ہے تو عقد لازم نہ ہو گا لیکن جب بچہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا تو اب وہ محض نفع رہ گیا کہ کام تو ختم ہو گیا صرف اجرت لینی باقی ہے تو اب اس عقد پر صحت کا حکم جاری کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ غلام مجور کی نظیر ہے کہ اگر وہ اپنے کو اجارہ پر دے دے تو جائز نہیں ہے اذن نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ لیکن جب وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا تو اب استحسانا عقد کی صحت کا حکم دے دیا جائے گا۔
تنبیہ - ملتقط بچہ کو اجارہ پر دینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا البتہ کوئی کام یکھنے کیلئے تعلیم کا اختیار ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے ان دونوں کو ایک سمجھ کر اجارہ پر دینے کو بھی جائز قرار دیا ہے حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے۔ ما ہو شامی ص ۲۵۰ ج۲
تنبیه ، باپ، دادا، قاضی کا بھی اجارہ پر دینا صحیح ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۵۰ ج ۲ باپ دادا، اجارہ پر ہے۔ شامی ۲۵ ج۲ ،
اور پھوپھی میں اختلاف ہے۔
The multaqit and uncle do not have the right to hire out the child. He (Imam Muhammad) said: It is not permissible for the multaqit to hire him out, but it is permissible for the mother to hire out her son if he is under her care, and it is not permissible for the uncle because the mother owns the power to waste his benefits by using him, unlike the multaqit and uncle. And if the child himself hires himself out, it is not permissible because it is mixed with harm, unless he has finished the work, because then it becomes purely beneficial, so the named wage becomes obligatory. It is analogous to the restricted slave who hires himself out, which we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage discusses the hiring out (ijara) of an orphan child. The ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is that the multaqit (finder) cannot hire out the child to work for others. The mother can, provided the child is under her care, because she has the right to utilize his services herself. The uncle cannot, nor can the father or grandfather? Actually the commentator adds that father, grandfather, and qadi can also hire out. The child himself cannot make a valid hiring contract because it involves both benefit and harm (he gets wages but loses freedom). However, if he has already completed the work, the contract becomes valid by istihsan because only the benefit (wage) remains. This is analogized to a restricted slave (a slave who is not permitted to trade) who hires himself out; the contract is initially invalid but becomes valid upon completion.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of hire where one person works for another for a specified wage.
عبد محجور ('abd maḥjūr): A slave who is restricted from making contracts independently, often because he is not given permission to trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad in the passage, when does a child's own hiring contract become valid?
A) Immediately upon the child's offer and acceptance
B) When the mother or guardian ratifies it
C) After the child has completed the entire work
D) It never becomes valid under any circumstance

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only those who legally own the child's benefits (mother, father, grandfather, qadi) may hire the child out; the multaqit and uncle cannot. A child's self-hiring is initially invalid but becomes valid upon completion of work by istihsan.
